“旺盛的精力对于我们是力量，但是在安宁、舒适的新环境下，这精力将会成为我们的弱势。即使在我们这个时代，某些倾向和欲望，曾经是生存所必须的，却通常会成为失败之源。比如，对一个文明之人来说，体力之勇和好战之心益处不大，甚至还可能是个障碍。在一个平稳安宁的国度，体力、智力以及权力都将是方枘圆凿。我估计，这个世界已经有数不清多少年都一直远离战争的威胁，没有专权的暴政，也不用担心有野兽的侵扰，没有什么使人消瘦的疾病，不需要强健的体格，人们也不需要辛苦劳作。对于这样一种生活来说，我们所称的弱者将和强者一样训练有素，弱者其实不再弱。实际上，他们还更具有优势，因为对于强者，如果他的精力得不到宣泄就会反生烦恼。毫无疑问，我见到的那些美轮美奂的建筑物是人类精力的最后一次迸发，这之后则归于平静，和他们生存的环境和谐共存。现在，精力再无存在的意义——在这一胜利之后便诞生了伟大的和平。这永远是安宁环境中精力的归宿。起初，它沉湎于艺术和情欲，而后变得萎靡不振，腐化衰落。 ‘Under the new conditions of perfect comfort and security, that restless energy, that with us is strength, would become weakness. Even in our own time certain tendencies and desires, once necessary to survival, area constant source of failure. Physical courage and the love of battle, for instance, are no great help—may even be hindrances—to a civilized man. And in a state of physical balance and security, power, intellectual as well as physical, would be out of place. For countless years I judged there had been no danger of war or solitary violence, no danger from wild beasts, no wasting disease to require strength of constitution, no need of toil. For such a life, what we should call the weak are as well equipped as the strong, are indeed no longer weak. Better equipped indeed they are, for the strong would be fretted by an energy for which there was no outlet. No doubt the exquisite beauty of the buildings I saw was the outcome of the last surgings of the now purposeless energy of mankind before it settled down into perfect harmony with the conditions under which it lived—the flourish of that triumph which began the last great peace. This has ever been the fate of energy insecurity; it takes to art and to eroticism, and then come languor and decay.
“即使这一追求艺术的冲动，最终也会消失——在我所看到的这一时代里，几乎都已经消亡了。他们用鲜花装扮自己，在阳光下唱歌，跳舞，这就是他们仅存的一点艺术火花，仅此而已。即使是那点火花，最终也会熄灭。到最后，他们对什么都不再感兴趣，却也心满意足。痛苦和需求的磨石不断磨砺出我们的锋芒，而在我看来，似乎那令人痛恶的磨石终于在这个时代也被打碎了！ ‘Even this artistic impetus would at last die away—had almost died in the Time I saw. To adorn themselves with flowers, to dance, to sing in the sunlight: so much was left of the artistic spirit, and no more. Even that would fade in the end into a contented inactivity. We are kept keen on the grindstone of pain and necessity, and, it seemed to me, that here was that hateful grindstone broken at last!
“天空愈加黑暗，我站在那里想到上面我的解释虽然简单，但是却抓住了世界的问题所在——掌握了这些可爱人们的全部秘密。也许他们抑制人口增长的办法非常奏效，导致人口不是保持稳定，而是有所下降了。这可以用来解释那些废墟是怎么一回事。我的解释很简单，听起来似乎也很有道理——正如大多数错误的理论一样！” ‘As I stood there in the gathering dark I thought that in this simple explanation I had mastered the problem of the world—mastered the whole secret of these delicious people. Possibly the checks they had devised for the increase of population had succeeded too well, and their numbers had rather diminished than kept stationary. That would account for the abandoned ruins. Very simple was my explanation, and plausible enough—as most wrong theories are!’
第五章 Chapter V
“我站在那里思索着人类所取得的这一超乎完美的胜利。东北部的天空中，一轮满月在一片银色的光辉中升起，像个黄色的圆盘。下面已看不到那些衣着鲜亮的小家伙们四处活动的身影，一只猫头鹰悄无声息地掠过身旁，夜晚的寒意让我禁不住打了一个冷颤。我决定下去找个可以睡觉的地方。 ‘As I stood there musing over this too perfect triumph of man, the full moon, yellow and gibbous, came up out of an overflow of silver light in the north-east. The bright little figures ceased to move about below, a noiseless owl flitted by, and I shivered with the chill of the night. I determined to descend and find where I could sleep.
“我找寻着自己认识的那座建筑，目光渐渐移到那个青铜底座的白色斯芬克斯雕像上。月光越来越明亮，雕像也更为清晰了，我还能看到与它相依的白桦树。在淡白的月光下，杂乱的杜鹃花丛只是一片黯淡，看不清颜色，还有那片小草坪。我又看了一眼草坪。一种莫名其妙的疑惑让刚才还得意的我立刻心灰意冷。‘不，’我斩钉截铁地对自己说，‘这不是之前的那个草坪。’ ‘I looked for the building I knew. Then my eye travelled along to the figure of the White Sphinx upon the pedestal of bronze, growing distinct as the light of the rising moon grew brighter. I could see the silver birch against it. There was the tangle of rhododendron bushes, black in the pale light, and there was the little lawn. I looked at the lawn again. A queer doubt chilled my complacency. “No,” said I stoutly to myself, “that was not the lawn.”
“但是它的确是那个草坪啊，因为那个斯芬克斯像麻风病一样苍白的脸就是面朝草坪的。你们能想象我确认无疑是这个草坪时的感受吗？不，你们肯定感受不到。时光机器不见了！ ‘But it was the lawn. For the white leprous face of the sphinx was towards it. Can you imagine what I felt as this conviction came home to me? But you cannot. The Time Machine was gone!
“我立刻像挨了当头一棒，想到有可能回不到自己的年代，将被孤立无助地丢在这陌生的世界。这一想法对我简直是极大的刺激，它扼住了我的咽喉，让我无法呼吸。不一会儿，我感到强烈的恐惧，大阔步向坡下跑去，中间不小心一头栽倒在地，划伤了脸。我来不及止住血，一跃而起，继续向前跑。我感到血沿着脸颊流到下巴，暖暖的。我一边跑一边对自己说：‘他们只是把时光机器稍微移动了一下，因为挡了路，把它推到了树丛下面。’但是我仍然全力奔跑着，心里一直坚信人有时往往会过于担心，我知道自己这一自信有多傻，直觉告诉我时光机器被搬走了，搬到我找不到的地方。我感觉呼吸时胸部疼痛起来。我估摸着自己从山顶一直跑到了小草坪，十分钟跑了大约有两英里。我已经不是年轻人了。我一边跑，一边大声诅咒自己满怀自信离开时光机器的愚蠢行为，因此浪费了好大力气。我大声哭喊，但没有一个人回应我。月光下，似乎连一个活动的身影都看不到。 ‘At once, like a lash across the face, came the possibility of losing my own age, of being left helpless in this strange new world. The bare thought of it was an actual physical sensation. I could feel it grip meat the throat and stop my breathing. In another moment I was in a passion of fear and running with great leaping strides down the slope. Once I fell headlong and cut my face; I lost no time in stanching the blood, but jumped up and ran on, with a warm trickle down my cheek and chin. All the time I ran I was saying to myself: “They have moved it a little, pushed it under the bushes out of the way.” Nevertheless, I ran with all my might. All the time, with the certainty that sometimes comes with excessive dread, I knew that such assurance was folly, knew instinctively that the machine was removed out of my reach. My breath came with pain. I suppose I covered the whole distance from the hillcrest to the little lawn, two miles perhaps, in ten minutes. And I am not a young man. I cursed aloud, as I ran, at my confident folly in leaving the machine, wasting good breath thereby. I cried aloud, and none answered. Not a creature seemed to be stirring in that moonlit world.
“当我跑到草坪的时候，我最担心的事情变成了现实。根本看不到时光机器的踪影。看着漆黑杂乱的树丛中这片空空的草坪，我感到头晕目眩，浑身冰冷。我围着它拼命跑，好像机器会被藏在某个角落，然后我突然停了下来，双手揪住头发。我仰头看到那个青铜底座上的雕像，冉冉升起的月光下白色的雕像闪着光晕，像患了麻风病的病人一样。它似乎是在嘲笑我的焦虑。 ‘When I reached the lawn my worst fears were realized. Not a trace of the thing was to be seen. I felt faint and cold when I faced the empty space among the black tangle of bushes. I ran round it furiously, as if the thing might be hidden in a corner, and then stopped abruptly, with my hands clutching my hair. Above me towered the sphinx, upon the bronze pedestal, white, shining, leprous, in the light of the rising moon. It seemed to smile in mockery of my dismay.
“要不是我确信那些小人儿的体力和智力水平都有限，我也许会想着是他们替我把机器放在一个安全的地方，以此来宽慰自己。正是因为确信他们没有那个力气和头脑，我才感到惊慌不安。我感到有某种目前还未知的力量介入，弄走了我的机器。但是，有一件事是确定的：机器不可能是去穿越时空了，除非某个别的时代也发明了完全相同的机器。我取下了操纵杆的配件，没有它，谁也不能启动机器去穿梭时空——我后面会给各位展示具体的操作方法。机器只是在空间上发生了位移，被藏在了某个地方。但问题是，它会在哪儿呢？ ‘I might have consoled myself by imagining the little people had put the mechanism in some shelter for me, had I not felt assured of their physical and intellectual inadequacy. That is what dismayed me: the sense of some hitherto unsuspected power, through whose intervention my invention had vanished. Yet, for one thing I felt assured: unless some other age had produced its exact duplicate, the machine could not have moved in time. The attachment of the levers—I will show you the method later—prevented any one from tampering with it in that way when they were removed. It had moved, and was hid, only in space. But then, where could it be?
“我想自己一定是有点发狂了。我记得自己发疯一般地闯进雕像四周月光笼罩下的树丛，又慌张地跑出来，惊动了某个白色的动物。在微弱的月光下，看着像是一头小鹿。我还记得那晚深夜，自己攥紧拳头敲打树丛，直到手指的关节被折断的细枝划破流血。极度痛苦中，我抽泣着，嘴里胡言乱语，向那座高大的石头建筑走去。荒废的大厅一片黑暗，寂静无人。因为地面不平，我滑了一跤，跌倒在一张孔雀石桌子上，差点折了胫骨。我点燃一根火柴，继续往前走，经过满是灰尘的窗帘——之前我跟你们讲过。 ‘I think I must have had a kind of frenzy. I remember running violently in and out among the moonlit bushes all round the sphinx, and startling some white animal that, in the dim light, I took for a small deer. I remember, too, late that night, beating the bushes with my clenched fist until my knuckles were gashed and bleeding from the broken twigs. Then, sobbing and raving in my anguish of mind, I went down to the great building of stone. The big hall was dark, silent, and deserted. I slipped on the uneven floor, and fell over one of the malachite tables, almost breaking my shin. I lit a match and went on past the dusty curtains, of which I have told you.
“往前走着，我又发现了一个大厅，大厅地上铺满了软垫，软垫上睡着大约二十来个人。伴随着的声音，还有火柴燃烧的劈啪声，我带着火柴的亮光突然从一片静寂的黑暗中冒了出来。我相信自己第二次出现的方式让他们感觉非常奇怪，因为他们早已忘记了火柴这个东西。‘我的时光机器呢？’我开始向他们发难，像一个生气的孩子一样喊叫着，两手抓住他们使劲摇晃，把他们都摇醒了。这也许让他们感到很奇怪。有些人笑了起来，但大多数看起来都吓坏了。当我看到他们站着围在我旁边，我突然意识到，在当时的情形下，自己的行为真是要多愚蠢有多愚蠢，我是在重新唤起他们的恐惧。因为，从他们白天的行为判断，我想他们一定是早就忘记了什么是恐惧。 ‘There I found a second great hall covered with cushions, upon which, perhaps, a score or so of the little people were sleeping. I have no doubt they found my second appearance strange enough, coming suddenly out of the quiet darkness with inarticulate noises and the splutter and flare of a match. For they had forgotten about matches. “Where is my Time Machine?” I began, bawling like an angry child, laying hands upon them and shaking them up together. It must have been very queer to them. Some laughed, most of them looked sorely frightened. When I saw them standing round me, it came into my head that I was doing as foolish a thing as it was possible for me to do under the circumstances, in trying to revive the sensation of fear. For, reasoning from their daylight behaviour, I thought that fear must be forgotten.
“突然，我扔掉火柴，跌跌撞撞地再次穿过大餐厅，走进月光之下的夜幕，往外走时不小心还撞倒了他们中的一个人。我听到身后他们恐惧的哭喊声，还有他们小脚磕磕绊绊地四处乱跑的声音。月亮缓缓地爬上天空，当时做过的一切我已经无法全部记起。我想是时光机器的意外丢失让我变得疯狂。想到和自己的同类从此隔绝，我感觉非常绝望，觉得自己就像一个闯入陌生世界的怪物。我当时肯定是走来走去地嚷嚷个不停，哭天抢地，诅咒命运。我记得自己是在绝望中疲惫不堪地度过了漫漫长夜，去了一个又一个不可能找到时光机器的地方，在月光下的废墟中摸索，还在黑影中触碰到一些奇怪的生物。最后，我在斯芬克斯像附近躺了下来，痛哭流涕。除了痛苦，我一无所有。后来，我睡着了。当我再醒来的时候，天已大亮，几只麻雀在我身旁的草坪上欢蹦乱跳，触手可及。 ‘Abruptly, I dashed down the match, and, knocking one of the people over in my course, went blundering across the big dining-hall again, out under the moonlight. I heard cries of terror and their little feet running and stumbling this way and that. I do not remember all I did as the moon crept up the sky. I suppose it was the unexpected nature of my loss that maddened me. I felt hopelessly cut off from my own kind—a strange animal in an unknown world. I must have raved to and fro, screaming and crying upon God and Fate. I have a memory of horrible fatigue, as the long night of despair wore away; of looking in this impossible place and that; of groping among moon-lit ruins and touching strange creatures in the black shadows; at last, of lying on the ground near the sphinx and weeping with absolute wretchedness. I had nothing left but misery. Then I slept, and when I woke again it was full day, and a couple of sparrows were hopping round me on the turf within reach of my arm.
“早晨空气清新，我坐起身来，试着回忆自己是怎么到那里的，为什么我会如此深深地感到孤独和绝望。接着，这些事情在我脑海中逐渐明朗起来。在白天真切、理性的光芒之下，我可以清楚地直面自己所面临的处境。我意识到自己昨天晚上的狂乱有多么愚蠢，并能够自己给自己分析眼下的情形。‘最坏的结果会是怎样？’我对自己说。‘假如说机器彻底消失了——也许被毁坏了？我应该静下心来，耐心一些，去领会这些人的行为方式，仔细想清楚我所丢机器的制作方法，以及如何获得材料和工具。这样到最后，也许我可以重新再造出一台时光机器。’那可能会是我最后的希望，不过怎么也好过绝望。而且，毕竟这还是一个美丽又奇特的世界。 ‘I sat up in the freshness of the morning, trying to remember how I had got there, and why I had such a profound sense of desertion and despair. Then things came clear in my mind. With the plain, reasonable daylight, I could look my circumstances fairly in the face. I saw the wild folly of my frenzy overnight, and I could reason with myself. “Suppose the worst?” I said. “Suppose the machine altogether lost—perhaps destroyed? It behooves me to be calm and patient, to learn the way of the people, to get a clear idea of the method of my loss, and the means of getting materials and tools; so that in the end, perhaps, I may make another.” That would be my only hope, perhaps, but better than despair. And, after all, it was a beautiful and curious world.
“但是，也有可能，机器只是被移走了。不过，我还是要保持冷静和耐心，找到它被藏在了哪里，或者强夺，或者智取，总之把它拿回来。这样想着，我赶紧爬起来，打量了一下自己，琢磨着到哪里去可以洗个澡。我感觉身心疲倦，浑身僵硬，满是尘土。清新的早晨使我也渴求同样清爽的身心。我已经耗尽了我所有的感情。真的，我一边着手找洗澡的地方，一边禁不住纳闷昨天晚上自己怎么会那么情绪激动。我在小草坪周围的地上仔细检查了一遍。我还询问了几个经过这里的人，尽我所能向他们表述我的意思，但结果都是白费力气，浪费时间。他们都没有看明白我的手势；一些人纯粹是置若罔闻，还有人以为我在和他们开玩笑，便冲我发笑。看着他们笑，我尽力遏制自己想在那些漂亮的脸蛋上动粗的冲动，这真是世界上最艰难的任务。我知道我这个冲动的想法很愚蠢，但是困惑之下，我几乎难以遏制心头的恐惧和无名怒火。草坪则给了我更好的提示。我发现就在斯芬克斯像的底座和我脚印中间的草坪上有一条撕裂开的凹槽，那脚印是我刚到这里时，奋力扶起翻倒的机器时留下的。周围还有其他一些移动的痕迹，地上有一些古怪的、细细的脚印，我猜想是树獭留下的。这些把我的注意力引向雕像的底座，我更加仔细地观察了一下。底座是青铜的，这个我想之前我也说过。它不只是一块简单的金属，而是每一面都精心装饰有带框的镶板。我走过去拍打了几下。那底座中间是空的。我仔细看了看那些镶板，我发现它们和边框不是紧密相连的。既没有把手，也没有锁眼，但是照我的猜想，如果这些镶板是门的话，可能是从里面开启的。有一件事我很清楚，不用费多少脑筋就能推断出，我的时光机器就在这个底座里。但是它是怎么跑到那里面去的就没那么容易想明白了。 ‘But probably, the machine had only been taken away. Still, I must be calm and patient, find its hiding-place, and recover it by force or cunning. And with that I scrambled to my feet and looked about me, wondering where I could bathe. I felt weary, stiff, and travel-soiled. The freshness of the morning made me desire an equal freshness. I had exhausted my emotion. Indeed, as I went about my business, I found myself wondering at my intense excitement overnight. I made a careful examination of the ground about the little lawn. I wasted sometime in futile questionings, conveyed, as well as I was able, to such of the little people as came by. They all failed to understand my gestures; some were simply stolid, some thought it was a jest and laughed at me. I had the hardest task in the world to keep my hands off their pretty laughing faces. It was a foolish impulse, but the devil begotten of fear and blind anger was ill curbed and still eager to take advantage of my perplexity. The turf gave better counsel. I found a groove ripped in it, about midway between the pedestal of the sphinx and the marks of my feet where, on arrival, I had struggled with the overturned machine. There were other signs of removal about, with queer narrow footprints like those I could imagine made by a sloth. This directed my closer attention to the pedestal. It was, as I think I have said, of bronze. It was not a mere block, but highly decorated with deep framed panels on either side. I went and rapped at these. The pedestal was hollow. Examining the panels with care I found them discontinuous with the frames. There were no handles or keyholes, but possibly the panels, if they were doors, as I supposed, opened from within. One thing was clear enough to my mind. It took no very great mental effort to infer that my Time Machine was inside that pedestal. But how it got there was a different problem.
“我看到两个穿橙色衣服的人穿过树丛，在花朵盛开的苹果树下朝我走来。我微笑着转向他们，并召唤他们过来。他们过来后，我手指青铜底座，试图向他们表示我想要打开底座。但是，一见我指向那个底座，他们就表现得非常奇怪。我不知道怎么给你描述他们的表情，试想你向一位敏感娇怯的女士做出非常不得体的动作，想想她会是什么表情你就知道了。他们都走开了，好像受到了莫大的耻辱。接着我又试着问一个穿着白色衣服，看起来很可爱的小家伙，得到的却也是完全相同的结果。不知为何，他的态度让我感到羞愧。但是，你们知道，我想要拿回时光机器，于是我再次向他表达我的意思。看到他也像其他人一样转身离开，我的脾气又上来了。我三个大阔步追上他，揪住他长袍宽松的领口，开始把他往雕像那儿拽。而后我看到他脸上露出极为恐惧和厌恶的表情，那一刹那我突然松开了手。 ‘I saw the heads of two orange-clad people coming through the bushes and under some blossom-covered apple-trees towards me. I turned smiling to them and beckoned them to me. They came, and then, pointing to the bronze pedestal, I tried to intimate my wish to open it. But at my first gesture towards this they behaved very oddly. I don’t know how to convey their expression to you. Suppose you were to use a grossly improper gesture to a delicate-minded woman—it is how she would look. They went off as if they had received the last possible insult. I tried a sweet-looking little chap in white next, with exactly the same result. Somehow, his manner made me feel ashamed of myself. But, as you know, I wanted the Time Machine, and I tried him once more. As he turned off, like the others, my temper got the better of me. In three strides I was after him, had him by the loose part of his robe round the neck, and began dragging him towards the sphinx. Then I saw the horror and repugnance of his face, and all of a sudden I let him go.
“但是，我还没有放弃。我用拳头砸那青铜镶板。我感觉听到里面有些动静——明确地说，我认为自己听到了像是咯咯发笑的声音——但是我一定是弄错了。接着，我在河里找到一大块鹅卵石，我拿着它捶打底座，直到把装饰上的螺旋纹都弄平了，底座表面的铜绿像粉末一样纷纷落下。那些娇小的人们无论是在我的哪一侧，肯定在一英里之外都听到了我这里一阵阵捶击的声音，但是他们什么反应都没有。我看到有一群人在山坡上，偷偷地看着我。最后，我感到又累又热，便坐下来看着这个地方。但是，我没法静下心来坐那看太久。我是个很西方化的人，长时间守夜这样的事我是做不来的。我可以花几年的时间钻研一个难题，却不会浪费二十四小时，什么都不做，干等在那里。 ‘But I was not beaten yet. I banged with my fist at the bronze panels. I thought I heard something stir inside—to be explicit, I thought I heard a sound like a chuckle—but I must have been mistaken. Then I got a big pebble from the river, and came and hammered till I had flattened a coil in the decorations, and the verdigris came off in powdery flakes. The delicate little people must have heard me hammering in gusty outbreaks a mile away on either hand, but nothing came of it. I saw a crowd of them upon the slopes, looking furtively at me. At last, hot and tired, I sat down to watch the place. But I was too restless to watch long; I am too Occidental for a long vigil. I could work at a problem for years, but to wait inactive for twenty-four hours—that is another matter.
“过了一会儿，我站起身，开始漫无目的地穿过树丛朝那座山走去。‘耐心，’我对自己说，‘如果你想找回时光机器就不能去管那个斯芬克斯雕像。如果他们真想要拿走你的机器，那你去毁坏他们的青铜镶板也没有多大意义，而如果他们并没有这个打算的话，你只要能向他们讲清楚就能把它要回来。置身于这个陌生的世界，面对那样的一个谜题，会感觉很无助，容易走向偏执。直面这个世界，领会它运作的方式，观察它，不要过于草率地猜测它的意图，最终你将会找出全部线索。’突然，我意识到自己现在的处境很可笑：想到自己花费几年时间潜心研究，费尽心力来到未来时代，现在又满心焦急地想要走出这个时代。我为自己设计了一个最为复杂和绝望的陷阱。尽管是我自作自受，可还是身不由己。想到这里，我不禁放声大笑。 ‘I got up after a time, and began walking aimlessly through the bushes towards the hill again. “Patience,” said I to myself. “If you you’re your machine again you must leave that sphinx alone. If they mean to take your machine away, it’s little good your wrecking their bronze panels, and if they don’t, you will get it back as soon as you can ask for it. To sit among all those unknown things before a puzzle like that is hopeless. That way lies monomania. Face this world. Learn its ways, watch it, be careful of too hasty guesses at its meaning. In the end you will find clues to it all.” Then suddenly the humour of the situation came into my mind: the thought of the years I had spent in study and toil to get into the future age, and now my passion of anxiety to get out of it. I had made myself the most complicated and the most hopeless trap that ever a man devised. Although it was at my own expense, I could not help myself. I laughed aloud.
“在走过大殿的时候，我感觉似乎那些人都在躲着我。也许是我瞎想，也许是跟我敲打底座的青铜门有关。不过我确定他们是在躲避我。尽管如此，我很谨慎，没有表现出有一丝在意，而且决不去追赶他们。一两天之后，一切又都恢复了正常。在语言上我取得了很大的进步。此外，我还四处探险。要么是我漏掉了一些细微之处，要么就是他们的语言极为简单——几乎全部是由实义名词和动词组成的。抽象名词即使有，似乎也极少，好像他们讲话中也不怎么使用修辞。他们的句子通常很简单，由两个词组成，我只能表述或是理解一些最简单的陈述。我决定先不去想时光机器和雕像下面青铜门的秘密，尽可能把它们留存在记忆深处，等到我逐步了解以后，我自然会重新考虑这些问题。然而，你们或许可以理解，我有一种感觉，问题的答案就在我到达之地这方圆几英里的范围之内。 ‘Going through the big palace, it seemed to me that the little people avoided me. It may have been my fancy, or it may have had something to do with my hammering at the gates of bronze. Yet I felt tolerably sure of the avoidance. I was careful, however, to show no concern and to abstain from any pursuit of them, and in the course of a day or two things got back to the old footing. I made what progress I could in the language, and in addition I pushed my explorations here and there. Either I missed some subtle point or their language was excessively simple—almost exclusively composed of concrete substantives and verbs. There seemed to be few, if any, abstract terms, or little use of figurative language. Their sentences were usually simple and of two words, and I failed to convey or understand any but the simplest propositions. I determined to put the thought of my Time Machine and the mystery of the bronze doors under the sphinx as much as possible in a corner of memory, until my growing knowledge would lead me back to them in a natural way. Yet a certain feeling, you may understand, tethered me in a circle of a few miles round the point of my arrival.
“目之所极，整个世界都像泰晤士河谷一样繁茂，富有生机。我每爬上一座山都能看到很多辉煌的建筑物。这些建筑的材料和风格都极尽差异，从每座山上都能看到簇拥生长的常绿植物灌木丛，以及开满鲜花的树木和蕨类植物。水光如银辉般到处闪耀。远处，大地隆起，绵延成一片起伏的群山，淡没于宁静的天际。一种奇特的景观立即吸引了我的注意。我看到了几口圆形的井，有几口看起来非常深。有一口井就在去往山上的小路旁，我第一次就是沿着这条小路走的。这口井和其他井一样，井口边缘用青铜围边，打造得十分奇特，井口上方有个小穹顶挡雨。我坐在这些井旁，凝视井下，只见里面一片漆黑，看不到一点水的微光，划亮一根火柴也没有看到有什么倒影。但是，我听到里面‘砰，砰，砰’的，像是什么发动机震动的声音。而且，借着火柴的光亮，我发现有一股稳定的气流下沉到井下。接着，我又把一个碎纸片扔进其中一口井里，那个小纸片不是飘飘晃晃地慢慢落下去，而是一下子就被吸进去，不见影了。 ‘So far as I could see, all the world displayed the same exuberant richness as the Thames valley. From every hill I climbed I saw the same abundance of splendid buildings, endlessly varied in material and style, the same clustering thickets of evergreens, the same blossom-laden trees and tree-ferns. Here and there water shone like silver, and beyond, the land rose into blue undulating hills, and so faded into the serenity of the sky. A peculiar feature, which presently attracted my attention, was the presence of certain circular wells, several, as it seemed to me, of a very great depth. One lay by the path up the hill, which I had followed during my first walk. Like the others, it was rimmed with bronze, curiously wrought, and protected by a little cupola from the rain. Sitting by the side of these wells, and peering down into the shafted darkness, I could see no gleam of water, nor could I start any reflection with a lighted match. But in all of them I heard a certain sound: a thud-thud-thud, like the beating of some big engine; and I discovered, from the flaring of my matches, that a steady current of air set down the shafts. Further, I threw a scrap of paper into the throat of one, and, instead of fluttering slowly down, it was at once sucked swiftly out of sight.
“过了一段时间，我把这些井和那些山坡上四处耸立的高塔联系起来，因为在那些高塔上方空气中都会有星光闪烁，就像艳阳天中被太阳烤得焦灼的沙滩上冒出的热气一样。将这些现象联系到一起，强烈地暗示出这是一个庞大的地下通风系统，而它真正的重要性却难以想象。一开始，我倾向于把它和这里人们的卫生清洁设施联想到一起。这个结论很容易得出，但绝对是错的。 ‘After a time, too, I came to connect these wells with tall towers standing here and there upon the slopes; for above them there was often just such a flicker in the air as one sees on a hot day above a sun-scorched beach. Putting things together, I reached a strong suggestion of an extensive system of subterranean ventilation, whose true import it was difficult to imagine. I was at first inclined to associate it with the sanitary apparatus of these people. It was an obvious conclusion, but it was absolutely wrong.
“这里，我必须承认，我在未来时代停留的那段时间里，对他们的排水管道、钟铃、各种交通运输方式以及类似的便利设施都几乎一无所知。在我所读到的一些关于乌托邦和未来时代的幻想著作中，有大量关于建筑物和社会公共设施的详细描述。如果整个世界尽在一个人的想象之中，这样的细节可以轻而易举地获得。然而，在我眼前的这个现实世界中，这些细节一个真正的旅行者却无法全都得到。试想一个刚从中非来到伦敦的黑人，会给他的部落带回一个怎样的伦敦经历！对于铁路公司、社会活动、电话线和电报线、邮递公司、汇单以及类似的东西，他能知道多少？然而，我们至少会十分乐意给他解释这些东西！即使是他知道的，他又能让他没有来过的朋友理解或相信多少呢？然后，想想我们这个时代一个黑人和白人之间的差距有多小，而我自己和这些黄金时代人们的间隔又是多么久远！我知道有很多使我感到安慰的东西我并未看到，但是，除了总体上感觉它是一个自动运作的体系以外，恐怕我给你们也讲不出其中有什么不同。 ‘And here I must admit that I learned very little of drains and bells and modes of conveyance, and the like conveniences, during my time in this real future. In some of these visions of Utopias and coming times which I have read, there is a vast amount of detail about building, and social arrangements, and so forth. But while such details are easy enough to obtain when the whole world is contained in one’s imagination, they are altogether inaccessible to a real traveller amid such realities as I found here. Conceive the tale of London which a negro, fresh from Central Africa, would take back to his tribe! What would he know of railway companies, of social movements, of telephone and telegraph wires, of the Parcels Delivery Company, and postal orders and the like? Yet we, at least, should be willing enough to explain these things to him! And even of what he knew, how much could he make his untravelled friend either apprehend or believe? Then, think how narrow the gap between a negro and a white man of our own times, and how wide the interval between myself and these of the Golden Age! I was sensible of much which was unseen, and which contributed to my comfort; but save for a general impression of automatic organization, I fear I can convey very little of the difference to your mind.
“比如，关于坟墓，我既看不到火葬场，也看不到任何能联想到坟墓的迹象。但是，我想到，也许在我所探索的区域之外可能会有墓地（或者火葬场）。这又是一个我刻意给自己提出的问题，一开始这个问题完全攫住了我的好奇心。我感到很困惑，这个问题把我引向又一个发现，这个发现让我更加迷惑：这些人中竟没有一个是年老体弱的。 ‘In the matter of sepulchre, for instance, I could see no signs of crematoria nor anything suggestive of tombs. But it occurred to me that, possibly, there might be cemeteries (or crematoria) somewhere beyond the range of my explorings. This, again, was a question I deliberately put to myself, and my curiosity was at first entirely defeated upon the point. The thing puzzled me, and I was led to make a further remark, which puzzled me still more: that aged and infirm among this people there were none.
“我必须承认，我对自己一开始提出的自动运作的文明和人性堕落的理论并没有满意太久。然而，我又想不出别的理论。让我详细说说我的难题。我探索的那几个大殿只不过是起居室、大餐厅和卧室。我找不到任何机器，也看不到任何一种器械。然而，这些人们却都穿着舒适的织物，肯定需要不时换新的，还有他们的凉鞋，尽管没有多少装饰，却也是非常复杂的金属器具加工品。这些东西肯定不会是凭空冒出来的，总是通过一定的手段制造的。但这些小人儿没有显示出有一丝创新的倾向。没有商店，没有工厂，也没看到他们之间有贸易往来的迹象。他们把全部时间都用来嬉戏，在河里游泳，半玩笑半认真地调情示爱，还有吃水果和睡觉。我看不出来他们的社会是怎么维持运行的。 ‘I must confess that my satisfaction with my first theories of an automatic civilization and a decadent humanity did not long endure. Yet I could think of no other. Let me put my difficulties. The several big palaces I had explored were mere living places, great dining-halls and sleeping apartments. I could find no machinery, no appliances of any kind. Yet these people were clothed in pleasant fabrics that must at times need renewal, and their sandals, though undecorated, were fairly complex specimens of metalwork. Somehow such things must be made. And the little people displayed no vestige of a creative tendency. There were no shops, no workshops, no sign of importations among them. They spent all their time in playing gently, in bathing in the river, in making love in a half-playful fashion, in eating fruit and sleeping. I could not see how things were kept going.
“接下来，还是关于我的时光机器。它被带进那座白色雕像的中空底座里去了，至于是被什么带进去的，我不知道。为什么要这么做？我穷尽一生也想象不出。还有那些并没有水的井，那些上面有气体隐隐闪烁的柱子。我觉得自己缺少一点线索。我感觉——该怎么跟你们说呢？试想你发现一些刻写的文字，句子基本都是优美易懂的英文，但是中间又穿插着其他一些你完全陌生的单词，甚至字母，你是什么感受？这正是在我造访那里的第三天，眼前的这个802701 年的世界带给我的感觉！ ‘Then, again, about the Time Machine: something, I knew not what, had taken it into the hollow pedestal of the White Sphinx. Why? For the life of me I could not imagine. Those waterless wells, too, those flickering pillars. I felt I lacked a clue. I felt—how shall I put it? Suppose you found an inscription, with sentences here and there in excellent plain English, and interpolated therewith, others made up of words, of letters even, absolutely unknown to you? Well, on the third day of my visit, that was how the world of Eight Hundred and Two Thousand Seven Hundred and One presented itself to me!
“同样是在那天，我交了一位朋友——勉强可以这么说。那天我正在看他们几个人在浅水处游泳嬉戏，其中一个抽筋了，开始往下游漂。水流相当急速，但即使对一个水性一般的人来说也不至于太过湍急。因此，如果我告诉你他们眼看着那个小家伙被淹，在水中无力地哭喊，却没有一个人做出哪怕一丁点的尝试去救她，你就会了解他们这一怪异的不足之处。当意识到他们没有一个人伸手相救，我便立刻脱掉衣服，在下游一个地方趟水下河，抓住那个可怜的小家伙，把她安全地拖到岸上。还好她没事，我揉搓了几下她的胳膊和腿，她很快恢复了知觉。在我离开她之前，看到她平安无事，我已经感到心满意足了。她的伙伴之前的表现让我对他们的看法跌到低谷，所以我并不指望她会有任何感激。然而，这下我可就错了。 ‘That day, too, I made a friend—of a sort. It happened that, as I was watching some of the little people bathing in a shallow, one of them was seized with cramp and began drifting downstream. The main current ran rather swiftly, but not too strongly for even a moderate swimmer. It will give you an idea, therefore, of the strange deficiency in these creatures, when I tell you that none made the slightest attempt to rescue the weakly crying little thing which was drowning before their eyes. When I realized this, I hurriedly slipped off my clothes, and, wading in at a point lower down, I caught the poor mite and drew her safe to land. A little rubbing of the limbs soon brought her round, and I had the satisfaction of seeing she was all right before I left her. I had got to such a low estimate of her kind that I did not expect any gratitude from her. In that, however, I was wrong.
“这是上午发生的事情。下午，我探险归来，返回到我的大本营时碰到了这个小妇人，我相信就是她。她欢呼着迎上来，送给我一个大花环——很明显是为我一个人做的。这东西让我浮想联翩, 很可能是由于我这几天一直感觉孤寂无望吧。不管怎样，我尽可能向她表示我很感谢她的礼物。不一会儿，我们就一起坐在一个小石亭里，相互交谈，主要是互致微笑。那个小家伙表示出的友好就像一个小孩一样，让我感动。我们彼此递花，她还亲吻我的双手，我也吻了吻她的手。然后，我试着跟她讲话，得知她的名字叫威娜，尽管我不知道这是什么意思，但是，不知为什么，觉得这名字似乎非常合适。就这样，我们开始了一段奇特的友情，维持了一个星期之后就结束了——后面我会给你们讲！ ‘This happened in the morning. In the afternoon I met my little woman, as I believe it was, as I was returning towards my centre1 from an exploration, and she received me with cries of delight and presented me with a big garland of f lowers—evidently made for me and meal one. The thing took my imagination. Very possibly I had been feeling desolate. At any rate I did my best to display my appreciation of the gift. We were soon seated together in a little stone arbour, engaged in conversation, chiefly of smiles. The creature’s friendliness affected me exactly as a child’s might have done. We passed each other f lowers, and she kissed my hands. I did the same to hers. Then I tried talk, and found that her name was Weena, which, though I don’t know what it meant, somehow seemed appropriate enough. That was the beginning of a queer friendship which lasted a week, and ended—as I will tell you!
“她简直就像一个小孩，总想跟我在一起，我到哪她都想跟着。等下一次外出探索的时候，我决心把她累倒，让她筋疲力尽，我再一走了之，让她跟在我后面悲悲切切地喊我。但是，这个世界的问题还需要弄明白。我对自己说，我来到未来世界不是来和这样的小家伙调情的。然而，我离开她的时候，她极为忧伤。分别时，她的叮嘱几近疯狂。我想，总的来说，她对我的挚爱在给了我莫大安慰的同时也给我带来不少麻烦。不过，不管怎样，她给予了我极大的慰藉。我以为她总是黏着我只是出于小孩子般情感的流露。我并不十分清楚当我离开她时给她造成了多大的痛苦，等我知道的时候已经晚了。同样，等我明白过来她对我的意义时也已经晚了。因为，她虽然只是流露出对我的喜爱，对我表示关心，尽管用处不大，但是仅凭这些，这个洋娃娃一样的家伙很快就让我感觉回到白色雕像附近简直像回到家一样。一翻过那座小山，我就留心找寻她白色和金色相间的瘦小身影。 ‘She was exactly like a child. She wanted to be with me always. She tried to follow me everywhere, and on my next journey out and about it went to my heart to tire her down, and leave her at last, exhausted and calling after me rather plaintively. But the problems of the world had to be mastered. I had not, I said to myself, come into the future to carry on a miniature flirtation. Yet her distress when I left her was very great, her expostulations at the parting were sometimes frantic, and I think, altogether, I had as much trouble as comfort from her devotion. Nevertheless she was, somehow, a very great comfort. I thought it was mere childish affection that made her cling to me. Until it was too late, I did not clearly know what I had inflicted upon her when I left her. Nor until it was too late did I clearly understand what she was to me. For, by merely seeming fond of me, and showing in her weak, futile way that she cared for me, the little doll of a creature presently gave my return to the neighbourhood of the White Sphinx almost the feeling of coming home; and I would watch for her tiny figure of white and gold so soon as I came over the hill.
“也是从她那里，我意识到恐惧还未从这个世界上消散。白天，她是无所畏惧的，而且她非常信任我，这种信任极为奇怪。有一次，我一时愚蠢，扮起鬼脸来恐吓她，却只引得她一阵大笑。但是她惧怕天黑，惧怕阴暗处，惧怕黑色的东西。她确实对黑暗十分恐惧。这种恐惧非常强烈，让我也开始琢磨并观察它。除了其他的一些现象，我还发现这些小家伙们天黑之后会聚集在那些大房子里，一群人一起睡觉。在黑暗中走到他们跟前会让他们恐惧得骚乱起来。我从来没有在天黑之后看到他们有哪个人还呆在室外或者独自一人睡在屋内。然而，我还是那么笨，没有从他们的恐惧中吸取教训，尽管威娜很难过，我还是坚持不和那群酣梦中的人睡在一起。 ‘It was from her, too, that I learned that fear had not yet left the world. She was fearless enough in the daylight, and she had the oddest confidence in me; for once, in a foolish moment, I made threatening grimaces at her, and she simply laughed at them. But she dreaded the dark, dreaded shadows, dreaded black things. Darkness to her was the one thing dreadful. It was a singularly passionate emotion, and it set me thinking and observing. I discovered then, among other things, that these little people gathered into the great houses after dark, and slept in droves. To enter upon them without a light was to put them into a tumult of apprehension. I never found one out of doors, or one sleeping alone within doors, after dark. Yet I was still such a blockhead that I missed the lesson of that fear, and in spite of Weena’s distress I insisted upon sleeping away from these slumbering multitudes.
“这可让威娜极为苦恼，但是最终她对我的奇特深情还是占了上风。我们认识的五个夜晚，包括即将永别的最后那一晚，她都是枕在我的胳膊上睡的。讲到她就忘了我的故事。一定是在救她的前一天晚上，天快亮的时候，我醒过来。我一晚上睡得都不安稳，梦到自己溺水，海葵用它们柔软的触须在我的脸上摩挲，真是个噩梦。我一下惊醒了，奇怪的是，恍惚间看到某个灰色的动物刚刚冲出了房间。我试着继续睡，但是感觉难以平静，很不舒服。那个时间，天刚蒙蒙亮，笼罩万物的黑暗正在消散，一切都暗淡无色，棱角分明，但却不真实。我不睡了，站起来，一直走进大厅，接着又出来，走到大殿前面的方石板上。我想既然别无选择，我不如欣然享受此刻，看看日出。 ‘It troubled her greatly, but in the end her odd affection for me triumphed, and for five of the nights of our acquaintance, including the last night of all, she slept with her head pillowed on my arm. But my story slips away from me as I speak of her. It must have been the night before her rescue that I was awakened about dawn. I had been restless, dreaming most disagreeably that I was drowned, and that sea anemones were feeling over my face with their soft palps. I woke with a start, and with an odd fancy that some greyish animal had just rushed out of the chamber. I tried to get to sleep again, but I felt restless and uncomfortable. It was that dim grey hour when things are just creeping out of darkness, when everything is colourless and clear cut, and yet unreal. I got up, and went down into the great hall, and so out upon the flagstones in front of the palace. I thought I would make a virtue of necessity, and see the sunrise.
“月亮渐渐下落，暗下去的月光和黎明第一道苍白的光线交织在一起，半明半暗之间令人害怕。矮树丛一团漆黑，大地灰暗，天空没有色彩，一片阴郁。我觉得往山上看可以看到幽灵。好几次，我的眼睛掠过山坡的时候，我都看到几个白色的影子。有两次，我好像看到了一个猿一样的白色动物向山上跑去，速度很快。还有一次，在那些废墟附近，我看到几只这种动物抬着一具黑色的尸体。他们动作很快，我没有看到后来他们怎样了，好像是消失在矮树丛中了。你要知道，天还只是蒙蒙亮，看不清楚。我感觉到清晨的凉意，还有那种浑浑噩噩的感觉，这些你们也许了解。因此，我怀疑起了自己的眼睛。 ‘The moon was setting, and the dying moonlight and the first pallor of dawn were mingled in a ghastly half-light. The bushes were inky black, the ground a sombre grey, the sky colourless and cheerless. And up the hill I thought I could see ghosts. There several times, as I scanned the slope, I saw white figures. Twice I fancied I saw a solitary white, ape-like creature running rather quickly up the hill, and once near the ruins I saw a leash of them carrying some dark body. They moved hastily. I did not see what became of them. It seemed that they vanished among the bushes. The dawn was still indistinct, you must understand. I was feeling that chill, uncertain, early-morning feeling you may have known. I doubted my eyes.
“东边的天空越来越明亮，白天的光亮和明艳的色彩重返大地。我仔细审视着四周，却一点也看不到那白色身影的踪迹。他们只是在天还没有亮的时候才活动。‘他们一定是幽灵，’我说，‘不知道他们是什么时候变成幽灵的。’这么说是因为我突然想到格兰特. 艾伦一个奇怪的观点，觉得很有趣。他说，如果每一代人死去都变成幽灵的话，世界最终会拥挤不堪。照这样，到80 万年之后，就会有难以计数的幽灵。我刚才同时看到四个也就不足为奇了。但是这个玩笑没能让我忘却烦恼，我一早上都在想那几个身影，直到从河里救下威娜才让我把这些抛到了脑后。那些身影让我模模糊糊地想到我第一次发疯一样寻找时光机器时惊动的一只白色动物。不过，威娜给我带来了快乐，让我忘记了这件事。但是，尽管如此，那些身影注定还是会很快地、更加彻底地占据我的大脑。 ‘As the eastern sky grew brighter, and the light of the day came on and its vivid colouring returned upon the world once more, I scanned the view keenly. But I saw no vestige of my white figures. They were mere creatures of the half light. “They must have been ghosts,” I said “I wonder whence they dated.” For a queer notion of Grant Allen’s2 came into my head, and amused me. If each generation die and leave ghosts, he argued, the world at last will get overcrowded with them. On that theory they would have grown innumerable some Eight Hundred Thousand Years hence, and it was no great wonder to see four at once. But the jest was unsatisfying, and I was thinking of these figures all the morning, until Weena’s rescue drove them out of my head. I associated them in some indefinite way with the white animal I had startled in my first passionate search for the Time Machine. But Weena was a pleasant substitute. Yet all the same, they were soon destined to take far deadlier possession of my mind.
“我想我之前说过这个黄金时代要比我们现在热得多。原因我也无法解释。可能是太阳释放的热量更多了，或是地球离太阳更近了。人们通常以为太阳的温度在未来会继续稳步下降，但是，人们对这些假设不甚熟悉，就像对达尔文年轻时代的假设无从了解一样，他们忽略了一点，那就是行星最终会一个个地回落到它们的母星体中。当这些灾难发生的时候，太阳就会用新生的能量燃烧，某个内行星或许已经遭遇了这样的灾难。不管是什么原因，事实就是太阳比我们现在的温度要高得多。 ‘I think I have said how much hotter than our own was the weather of this Golden Age. I cannot account for it. It may be that the sun was hotter, or the earth nearer the sun. It is usual to assume that the sun will go on cooling steadily in the future. But people, unfamiliar with such speculations as those of the younger Darwin, forget that the planets must ultimately fall back one by one into the parent body. As these catastrophes occur, the sun will blaze with renewed energy; and it maybe that some inner planet had suffered this fate. Whatever the reason, the fact remains that the sun was very much hotter than we know it.
“在一个酷热的早晨——我想，是我在那里的第四天——天气炎热，阳光刺眼。在我吃饭、睡觉的那个大房子附近有一片巨大的废墟，我正想在废墟里找个凉快点的地方，不料在那里碰到一件怪事：我正吃力地在这些砖石堆中攀爬，突然发现一条狭窄的通道，通道尽头和两边的窗户被倒塌下来的乱石堵住了。和外面的阳光明媚相比较，那通道起初在我眼前就是一片无法穿越的黑暗。我摸索着走进去，从外面的阳光世界一下扎进这黑漆一片的走廊，让我眼前出现了些跳动的光点。突然，我像是被念了咒语一样停住了。黑暗中，只见一对眼睛在外面日光的反射下闪闪发亮，正盯着我看。 ‘Well, one very hot morning—my fourth, I think—as I was seeking shelter from the heat and glare in a colossal ruin near the great house where I slept and fed, there happened this strange thing: Clambering among these heaps of masonry, I found a narrow gallery, whose end and side windows were blocked by fallen masses of stone. By contrast with the brilliancy outside, it seemed at first impenetrably dark to me. I entered it groping, for the change from light to blackness made spots of colour swim before me. Suddenly I halted spellbound. A pair of eyes, luminous by reflection against the daylight without, was watching me out of the darkness.
“对野兽本能的恐惧悄悄涌上心头。我攥紧拳头，紧紧盯着那双闪光的眼珠。我怕得不敢转身。接着，我想到了那时的人类看起来生活得十分安宁，完全没有什么威胁，接着又想起他们对黑暗的那种奇怪的畏惧。稍稍镇住了恐惧，我向前迈了一步，开口讲话。我承认我的声音很粗暴，一点儿也不客气。我伸出手，碰到了什么柔软的东西。那双眼睛的目光立刻转向一边，我看到一个白色的东西从身边跑过。我转过身来，吓得心提到了嗓子眼儿，我看到一个奇怪的像猿一样的小身影，它的脑袋奇怪地低垂着，迅速跑过我身后的阳光地带。它撞到了一块花岗岩上，踉跄到一边，不一会儿就消失在另一堆砖石废墟的黑暗中。 ‘The old instinctive dread of wild beasts came upon me. I clenched my hands and steadfastly looked into the glaring eyeballs. I was afraid to turn. Then the thought of the absolute security in which humanity appeared to be living came to my mind. And then I remembered that strange terror of the dark. Overcoming my fear to some extent, I advanced a step and spoke. I will admit that my voice was harsh and ill-controlled. I put out my hand and touched something soft. At once the eyes darted sideways, and something white ran past me. I turned with my heart in my mouth, and saw a queer little ape-like figure, its head held down in a peculiar manner, running across the sunlit space behind me. It blundered against a block of granite, staggered aside, and in a moment was hidden in a black shadow beneath another pile of ruined masonry.
“它留给我的印象当然不是那么完整，但是我知道它颜色暗白，有一双红色的大眼睛，略带灰色，很是奇怪。它头上和后背下方的毛发是淡黄色的。但是，正如我所说的，它跑得太快了，我来不及看清楚。我都说不出它是四肢着地跑，还是只将两个前肢放得很低而已。犹豫了一下，我跟着它进了第二堆废墟。一开始我找不到它，但是过了一会儿，在一处极为幽暗的地方，我走到了一个像井一样的圆口前，前面我也提到过，它的圆形口被一个倒塌的柱子半遮着。我脑海中突然闪出一个想法：那个东西有没有可能消失在这下面了？我点燃一根火柴，朝下看，我看到一个白色的小东西正在挪动。它一边往下面退，一边用它又大又亮的眼睛注视着我，看得我浑身战栗。它真像一个蜘蛛人！它沿着墙壁往下爬，我这才注意到沿着井壁往下，有许多金属物，可以扶手或撑脚，像梯子一样。这时火柴烧到了我的手指，从手中掉了下去，熄灭了。等我再擦亮一根时，那小东西已经不见了。 ‘My impression of it is, of course, imperfect; but I know it was a dull white, and had strange large greyish-red eyes; also that there was flaxen hair on its head and down its back. But, as I say, it went too fast for me to see distinctly. I cannot even say whether it ran on all-fours, or only with its forearms held very low. After an instant’s pause I followed it into the second heap of ruins. I could not find it at first; but, after a time in the profound obscurity, I came upon one of those round well like openings of which I have told you, half closed by a fallen pillar. A sudden thought came to me. Could this Thing have vanished down the shaft? I lit a match, and, looking down, I saw a small, white, moving creature, with large bright eyes which regarded me steadfastly as it retreated. It made me shudder. It was so like a human spider! It was clambering down the wall, and now I saw for the first time a number of metal foot and hand rests forming a kind of ladder down the shaft. Then the light burned my fingers and fell out of my hand, going out as it dropped, and when I had lit another the little monster had disappeared.
“我不知道自己坐在那里，往井下凝视了多久。我好一阵子都无法说服自己相信我看到的那个东西是个人。但是渐渐地，我明白了真相：人类不再是一个物种，而是进化成两种截然不同的动物，也就是说，地上世界那些优雅可爱的小家伙们不是我们唯一的后代，从我眼前一闪而过的这个令人厌恶的白色夜行动物同样是我们的后裔。 ‘I do not know how long I sat peering down that well. It was not for some time that I could succeed in persuading myself that the thing I had seen was human. But, gradually, the truth dawned on me: that Man had not remained one species, but had differentiated into two distinct animals: that my graceful children of the Upper-world were not the sole descendants of our generation, but that this bleached, obscene, nocturnal Thing, which had flashed before me, was also heir to all the ages.
“我想到那些上面有气体飘曳的柱子，还有我关于地下通风系统的看法。我开始怀疑它们的真实用途。不知道这种狐猴一样的东西在这个我认为完美宁静的世界里做些什么呢？它和上面那些漂亮的人们懒散恬静的生活有什么关系吗？那个井底又隐藏着什么？我坐在井沿对自己说，不管怎样，没什么可怕的，为了解决我的难题我必须下去。可我又绝对不敢下去！正当我犹豫不决时，两个上面世界的人在背光处你追我跑，很是亲昵。女的在前，男的在后，男的边跑边朝那女的扔花。 ‘I thought of the flickering pillars and of my theory of an underground ventilation. I began to suspect their true import. And what, I wondered, was this Lemur doing in my scheme of a perfectly balanced organization? How was it related to the indolent serenity of the beautiful Upper-worlders? And what was hidden down there, at the foot of that shaft? I sat upon the edge of the well telling myself that, at any rate, there was nothing to fear, and that there I must descend for the solution of my difficulties. And withal I was absolutely afraid to go! As I hesitated, two of the beautiful Upper-world people came running in their amorous sport across the daylight in the shadow. The male pursued the female, flinging flowers at her as he ran.
“看到我一只胳膊撑在井口倒下的柱子上，凝视着井下，他们似乎很痛苦的样子。显而易见，我是不该朝这里看的。当我用手指着井，试着用他们的语言问一个关于这个井的问题时，他们脸上的痛苦表情更为明显，还别过脸去不看我。但是他们对我的火柴很感兴趣，我划了几根逗他们开心。我又试着问那个井，结果还是没成功。于是，过了会儿，我离开了他们，想要回到威娜那里，看看从她那里能不能找到答案。但是我的思想已经发生了根本性的变化；我已经有了新的猜测和判断。现在，对于这些井的意义，那些通风的高塔，神秘的幽灵，我都已掌握了一些线索。至于那青铜门是做什么用的，还有时光机器去了哪里就更有把握了！对于他们如何解决经济问题，我早就感到困惑，现在隐约也得到了一些启示。 ‘They seemed distressed to find me, my arm against the overturned pillar, peering down the well. Apparently it was considered bad form to remark these apertures; for when I pointed to this one, and tried to frame a question about it in their tongue, they were still more visibly distressed and turned away. But they were interested by my matches, and I struck some to amuse them. I tried them again about the well, and again I failed. So presently I left them, meaning to go back to Weena, and see what I could get from her. But my mind was already in revolution; my guesses and impressions were slipping and sliding to a new adjustment. I had now a clue to the import of these wells, to the ventilating towers, to the mystery of the ghosts; to say nothing of a hint at the meaning of the bronze gates and the fate of the Time Machine! And very vaguely there came a suggestion towards the solution of the economic problem that had puzzled me.
“我的新看法是这样的：第二种人类明显是生活在地下的。有三点特别之处使我觉得它很少出现在地上是由于长时间习惯于地下活动造成的：首先，大多数生活在黑暗中的动物颜色都发白。例如，肯塔基州洞穴中白色的鱼；此外，它的眼睛很大，可以反射光线，这是夜行动物的共同特征——看看猫头鹰和猫就知道了；最后，它在阳光下明显陷入混乱，慌乱地摸索着，跌跌撞撞逃回黑暗之中，还有它在光照下头部低垂的奇怪姿态——这些都进一步证明它的视网膜极为敏感。 ‘Here was the new view. Plainly, this second species of Man was subterranean. There were three circumstances in particular which made me think that its rare emergence above ground was the out come of a long-continued underground habit. In the first place, there was the bleached look common in most animals that live largely in the dark—the white fish of the Kentucky caves, for instance. Then, those large eyes, with that capacity for reflecting light, are common features of nocturnal things—witness the owl and the cat. And last of all, that evident confusion in the sunshine, that hasty yet fumbling awkward flight towards dark shadow, and that peculiar carriage of the head while in the light—all reinforced the theory of an extreme sensitiveness of the retina.
“就在我脚下，一定布满了大量的地下通道，这些通道就是这一新种人类的栖息地。山坡上的通风塔和井口可以表明这些地下通道的分布范围之广——事实上，除了河谷一带，到处都能看到。那么，也就很自然地想到：是不是这个人造的地下世界完成了必要的工作以保障阳光下的种族生活得舒适安逸呢？这个想法貌似很合理，以至于我立刻就相信了，并且还继续猜想着人类是怎样分离成两个种群的。我敢说你们会料到我的看法，但是我自己很快就感到事实远非如此。 ‘Beneath my feet, then, the earth must be tunneled enormously, and these tunnellings were the habitat of the new race. The presence of ventilating shafts and wells along the hill slopes—everywhere, in fact except along the river valley—showed how universal were its ramifications. What so natural, then, as to assume that it was in this artificial Underworld that such work as was necessary to the comfort of the daylight race was done? The notion was so plausible that I at once accepted it, and went on to assume the how of this splitting of the human species. I dare say you will anticipate the shape of my theory; though, for myself, I very soon felt that it fell far short of the truth.
“首先，从我们自己时代的各种问题说起，资本家和工人间目前的社会差距还仅仅是暂时的，但却正在逐步拉大。在我看来，很明显这就是整个形势的关键所在。不用说，你肯定会觉得这十分荒诞，而且难以置信！但即使是现在，也还存在一些情形证明事实确实如此。现在有这样一种趋势，就是利用地下空间去发展文明社会中那些无需装饰的行业。例如，伦敦有大都会铁路，有新型电气铁路，有地铁，还有地下工厂和饭店，而且它们的数量还在不断增加。我认为，明显可以看出这种趋势持续见长，直到工业在地上逐渐丧失其生存的空间。我的意思是，它已经越来越深入，地下工厂也发展得越来越庞大，越来越多的工业在地下完成，直到最后——！就说现在，伦敦东区的工人不就是生活在这样的人造世界里，几乎与地面上的自然世界相隔绝了吗？ ‘At first, proceeding from the problems of our own age, it seemed clear as daylight to me that the gradual widening of the present merely temporary and social difference between the Capitalist and the Labourer, was the key to the whole position. No doubt it will seem grotesque enough to you—and wildly incredible!—and yet even now there are existing circumstances to point that way. There is a tendency to utilize underground space for the less ornamental purposes of civilization; there is the Metropolitan Railway in London, for instance, there are new electric railways, there are subways, there are underground workrooms and restaurants, and they increase and multiply. Evidently, I thought, this tendency had increased till Industry had gradually lost its birthright in the sky. I mean that it had gone deeper and deeper into larger and ever larger underground factories, spending a still-increasing amount of its time therein, till, in the end—! Even now, does not an East-end worker live in such artificial conditions as practically to be cut off from the natural surface of the earth?
“此外，毫无疑问，由于富人所受的教育日益完善，以及他们和穷人粗鲁的暴力行为之间隔阂的日渐加深，形成富人独占一切的倾向。他们为了自己的利益，已经将地面上相当大的一部分土地瓜分殆尽。比如说伦敦，大约一半风景怡人的乡村都已经被锁闭，不得踏入。富人和穷人间的这一鸿沟日益加深，原因一方面在于高等教育期限长，费用高，另外还因为越来越多的诱惑使富人趋向于精致优雅的生活，也有更多的设施服务于他们的这种生活习惯。这鸿沟将使富人和穷人间的交流越来越少，尽管两个阶层间的通婚本来可以延缓种族间的分裂，但是后来也变得越来越罕见了。因此，最终必然会产生地上的富人和地下的穷人。富人图乐求美，追求安逸，而地下那些贫穷的工人们则要不断适应他们的劳动环境。工人们一旦到了地下世界，就毫无疑问要支付租金，其中有不少一部分是他们所居地洞的通风费用。如果他们拒绝支付的话，就会因为拖欠而挨饿或窒息得透不过气。他们当中那些贫困的和反叛的人会死去。最后实现一种永久的平衡，地上地下安然相处。那些幸存下来的会像地上人享受他们的生活那样，习惯于他们的地下生活，并且乐在其中。在我看来，这里地上人的精致美丽和地下种族的苍白面色是顺利成章的。 ‘Again, the exclusive tendency of richer people—due, no doubt, to the increasing refinement of their education, and the widening gulf between them and the rude violence of the poor—is already leading to the closing, in their interest, of considerable portions of the surface of the land. About London, for instance, perhaps half the prettier country is shut in against intrusion. And this same widening gulf—which is due to the length and expense of the higher educational process and the increased facilities for and temptations towards refined habits on the part of the rich—will make that exchange between class and class, that promotion by intermarriage which at present retards the splitting of our species along lines of social stratification, less and less frequent. So, in the end, above ground you must have the Haves, pursuing pleasure and comfort and beauty, and below ground the Have-nots, the Workers getting continually adapted to the conditions of their labour. Once they were there, they would no doubt have to pay rent, and not a little of it, for the ventilation of their caverns; and if they refused, they would starve or be suffocated for arrears. Such of them as were so constituted as to be miserable and rebellious would die; and, in the end, the balance being permanent, the survivors would become as well adapted to the conditions of underground life, and as happy in their way, as the Upper-world people were to theirs. As it seemed to me, the refined beauty and the etiolated pallor followed naturally enough.
“我曾梦想的人性的伟大胜利在我脑海中成了另一幅景象。它没有我想象中的那种道德教育和全面合作的胜利。相反，我看到了一个真正的贵族阶级，他们的科技水平几近完美，正在把我们今天的工业系统最终推向一个合乎逻辑的结局。他们的胜利不仅在于征服了自然，而是对自然还有他们同胞的双重征服。不过，我必须提醒你们，这是我当时的看法。我没有从描写乌托邦的一类书籍中得到什么可以直接用的指导思想。我的解释可能完全是错误的，不过我仍旧觉得它似乎是最有道理的。但即使是依照这个推测，最终取得平衡的文明也必然已经早走过了它的巅峰时期，现在已经一落千丈，陷入衰退了。地上世界的人们生活太过安逸，导致他们走向缓慢的退化。他们的身材变小，力量变弱，智力降低。这些我早已清楚地看在眼里。地下世界的人经历了怎样的变化我还猜不出来，但是从我对莫洛克斯人的观察来看，可以想象他们的变异比‘埃洛伊人’更为巨大。这里顺便提一下，莫洛克斯人是对地下种族的称呼，‘埃洛伊人’是指我已经了解的那个漂亮的种族。 ‘The great triumph of Humanity I had dreamed of took a different shape in my mind. It had been no such triumph of moral education and general co-operation as I had imagined. Instead, I saw a real aristocracy, armed with a perfected science and working to a logical conclusion the industrial system of today. Its triumph had not been simply a triumph over Nature, but a triumph over Nature and the fellow-man. This, I must warn you, was my theory at the time. I had no convenient cicerone in the pattern of the Utopian books. My explanation may be absolutely wrong. I still think it is the most plausible one. But even on this supposition the balanced civilization that was at last attained must have long since passed its zenith, and was now far fallen into decay. The too-perfect security of the Upper-worlders had led them to a slow movement of degeneration, to a general dwindling in size, strength, and intelligence. That I could see clearly enough already. What had happened to the Under-grounders I did not yet suspect; but from what I had seen of the Morlocks—that, by the by, was the name by which these creatures were called—I could imagine that the modification of the human type was even far more profound than among the “Eloi,” the beautiful race that I already knew.
“现在，棘手的问题来了。莫洛克斯人为什么要拿走我的时光机器呢？我肯定是他们拿走的。而如果埃洛伊人是主人的话，为什么不能拿回我的机器呢？另外，他们为什么那么害怕黑暗呢？像我前面提到的那样，我继续问威娜关于地下世界的问题，但我依旧没有得到答案。一开始，她不明白我的问题，后来她又不愿回答。她颤抖着，好像这个话题让她无法忍受。接着，当我逼问她时，也许是我有些严厉，她突然哭了起来。这是我在这个黄金时代唯一一次看到眼泪，我自己的除外。看到她哭了，我立刻不再追问关于莫洛克斯的问题，只想着替威娜擦掉眼泪，这泪水也是人类遗传的迹象。当我面色凝重地擦亮一根火柴，她很快就笑逐颜开，拍起了小手。” ‘Then came troublesome doubts. Why had the Morlocks taken my Time Machine? For I felt sure it was they who had taken it. Why, too, if the Eloi were masters, could they not restore the machine to me? And why were they so terribly afraid of the dark? I proceeded, as I have said, to question Weena about this Under-world, but here again I was disappointed. At first she would not understand my questions, and presently she refused to answer them. She shivered as though the topic was unendurable. And when I pressed her, perhaps a little harshly, she burst into tears. They were the only tears, except my own, I ever saw in that Golden Age. When I saw them I ceased abruptly to trouble about the Morlocks, and was only concerned in banishing these signs of the human inheritance from Weena’s eyes. And very soon she was smiling and clapping her hands, while I solemnly burned a match.’
1 大本营，这里指时光旅行者的中心区域，即狮身人面像附近的区域。2 格兰特. 艾伦（1848—1899），生于加拿大，19世纪科幻作家、小说家，是进化论的拥护者。
第六章 Chapter VI
“可能你们会觉得奇怪，但我的确是过了两天后，才得以找到明显合适的方式继续跟进新发现的线索。我感到自己对那些苍白的东西有种特别的畏缩情绪。他们就像你们在动物博物馆里看到的那些泡在酒精里的软体爬虫，还有动物标本一样，呈半漂白的颜色，摸上去冰凉又肮脏。我退避他们可能很大程度上是受埃洛伊人的影响，我现在开始理解他们对莫洛克斯人的厌恶。 ‘It may seem odd to you, but it was two days before I could follow up the new-found clue in what was manifestly the proper way. I felt a peculiar shrinking from those pallid bodies. They were just the half bleached colour of the worms and things one sees preserved in spirit in a zoological museum. And they were filthily cold to the touch. Probably my shrinking was largely due to the sympathetic influence of the Eloi, whose disgust of the Morlocks I now began to appreciate.
“接下来的那天晚上，我没有睡好。可能我身体有点不舒服，困惑和疑虑使我的心情沉闷。有一两次，我感到极度的恐惧，却又说不清到底在害怕什么。我记得有一晚，自己在月光下悄悄爬到那些人睡觉的大厅，威娜也在其中，看到他们我才感到心安。那时，我甚至想到，再过几天，等最后那一弯月牙也没有了，夜幕降临后一片黑暗。那时，这些令人厌恶的地下生物，这些白色的狐猴，这种替代了旧品种的新害虫可能会更为猖獗。这两天，我都有一种坐立不安的感觉，像是在逃避一个不可推卸的责任。我肯定只有勇敢地进入神秘的地下世界才能找回我的时光机器，但是我却不敢面对这个神秘的世界。要是我能有一个同伴，那情况就截然不同了。但是，我形单影只，多可怕啊，即使是爬到黑暗的井下也让我胆颤心惊。我不知道你们是否理解我的感受，但我从来没感到背后安全过。 ‘The next night I did not sleep well. Probably my health was a little disordered. I was oppressed with perplexity and doubt. Once or twice I had a feeling of intense fear for which I could perceive no definite reason. I remember creeping noiselessly into the great hall where the little people were sleeping in the moonlight—that night Weena was among them—and feeling reassured by their presence. It occurred to me even then, that in the course of a few days the moon must pass through its last quarter, and the nights grow dark, when the appearances of these unpleasant creatures from below, these whitened Lemurs, this new vermin that had replaced the old, might be more abundant. And on both these days I had the restless feeling of one who shirks an inevitable duty. I felt assured that the Time Machine was only to be recovered by boldly penetrating these underground mysteries. Yet I could not face the mystery. If only I had had a companion it would have been different. But I was so horribly alone, and even to clamber down into the darkness of the well appalled me. I don’t know if you will understand my feeling, but I never felt quite safe at my back.
“也许，正是这种焦虑和惶恐才驱使我走向更远的地方去探险。我朝西南方向走去，现在，那个方向是一个叫做峡谷树林的坡地地区。向稍远的方向望去，在19世纪班斯代德镇的方向，我看到一片广袤的绿色建筑，其外部特征与我之前见到的任何建筑都有所不同。它比我知道的最大的宫殿或遗迹还要高大，它的正面看上去是东方式的外观：淡绿色的表面带有光泽，那是一种青绿色，有点像中国瓷器的颜色。这种外观上的差异可能说明它有不同的用途，我打算继续探索。但是，时间不早了，我走了一大圈才到这个地方，也很疲惫了，因此我打算第二天再继续探索，就回到小威娜那里。她轻轻地爱抚我，迎接我回来。但是第二天早上，我清楚地意识到我对那个绿瓷器宫殿的兴趣只是自欺欺人，我只是借它又逃避一天，躲过我不敢冒险去做的那件事。我决定不再浪费时间，我要下井看看。一大早我就出发了，那个夹杂着铝和花岗岩的废墟附近有一口井，我就朝那儿走去。 ‘It was this restlessness, this insecurity, perhaps, that drove me further and further afield in my exploring expeditions. Going to the south-westward towards the rising country that is now called Combe Wood, I observed far off, in the direction of nineteenth-century Banstead1, a vast green structure, different in character from any I had hitherto seen. It was larger than the largest of the palaces or ruins I knew, and the facade had an Oriental look: the face of it having the lustre, as well as the pale-green tint, a kind of bluish-green, of a certain type of Chinese porcelain. This difference in aspect suggested a difference inuse, and I was minded to push on and explore. But the day was growing late, and I had come upon the sight of the place after a long and tiring circuit; so I resolved to hold over the adventure for the following day, and I returned to the welcome and the caresses of little Weena. But next morning I perceived clearly enough that my curiosity regarding the Palace of Green Porcelain was a piece of self-deception, to enable me to shirk, by another day, an experience I dreaded. I resolved I would make the descent without further waste of time, and started out in the early morning towards a well near the ruins of granite and aluminium.
“小威娜跟着我去了。她在我旁边蹦啊跳啊的，一直到那口井边，但是当她看到我俯身井口往下看的时候，她奇怪地惊慌起来。‘再见，小威娜。’说着，我吻了吻她，然后，我放下她，把手伸到井边，摸索着井壁的扶手。我得承认，自己是急急忙忙地往下爬，因为我生怕鼓起的勇气会溜走。威娜一开始惊奇地看着我，接着，她极为凄惨地哭着跑向我，用她那双小手拽着我。我想她的阻止反倒使我有胆量往下爬。我甩开她，可能稍微有些粗鲁。过了片刻，我已经置身井内。我看到她在井边痛苦的表情，便笑了笑宽慰她。之后，我就得低头看着井壁上自己牢牢抓着的扶手，它们并不牢固。 ‘Little Weena ran with me. She danced beside me to the well, but when she saw me lean over the mouth and look downward, she seemed strangely disconcerted. “Good-bye, Little Weena,” I said, kissing her; and then putting her down, I began to feel over the parapet for the climbing hooks. Rather hastily, I may as well confess, for I feared my courage might leak away! At first she watched me in amazement. Then she gave a most piteous cry, and running to me, she began to pull at me with her little hands. I think her opposition nerved me rather to proceed. I shook her off, perhaps a little roughly, and in another moment I was in the throat of the well. I saw her agonized face over the parapet, and smiled to reassure her. Then I had to look down at the unstable hooks to which I clung.
“我得往井下爬大概二百码的距离。我是借助井壁四周突出的金属横杆往下爬的。那些地下生物比我小得多，也轻得多，这些横杆适应他们的身形特点，因此往下爬了没多久我就感到很局促，疲倦。还不仅仅是累！其中一个杆子在我的重压下突然往下一弯，差点把我晃到脚下的黑暗之中。我一只手抓着横杆在那里吊了一会儿。经过这次惊险，我再也不敢休息片刻。尽管没过多久我就感到两臂和后背剧烈的酸痛，可还是尽可能迅速地往下爬。我仰头往上看，只见井口成了一个蓝色的小圆盘，有一颗星星清晰可见，而小威娜的头在天空的映衬下像一个黑色的圆影。地下传来机器砰砰的声音，越来越大，越来越沉闷。除了井口那一点蓝色的天空，周围伸手不见五指，当我再往上看的时候，威娜已经不见了。 ‘I had to clamber down a shaft of perhaps two hundred yards. The descent was effected by means of metallic bars projecting from the sides of the well, and these being adapted to the needs of a creature much smaller and lighter than myself, I was speedily cramped and fatigued by the descent. And not simply fatigued! One of the bars bent suddenly under my weight, and almost swung me off into the blackness beneath. For a moment I hung by one hand, and after that experience I did not dare to rest again. Though my arms and back were presently acutely painful, I went on clambering down the sheer descent with as quick a motion as possible. Glancing upward, I saw the aperture, a small blue disk, in which a star was visible, while little Weena’s head showed as around black projection. The thudding sound of a machine below grew louder and more oppressive. Everything save that little disk above was profoundly dark, and when I looked up again Weena had disappeared.
“我感觉非常难受，想过再试着爬上去，管它什么地下世界。但即使是我脑海中认真考虑着这一想法，我还是不停地往下爬。最后，我隐约看到在我右侧一英尺远的井壁上有一个狭长的小洞，我如释重负。摆身进了那个洞口，我发现这是一个狭窄的横向地道的洞口，我可以在里面躺下休息一会儿。从上面爬下来时间并不短，我的胳膊酸疼，后背一阵痉挛。从上面往下爬时，一直害怕跌下去，长时间的紧张让我不禁颤抖。此外，持续的黑暗折磨着我的眼睛。空气中回响着机器往井下抽气发出的隆隆声和嗡嗡声。 ‘I was in an agony of discomfort. I had some thought of trying to go up the shaft again, and leave the Under-world alone. But even while I turned this over in my mind I continued to descend. At last, within tense relief, I saw dimly coming up, a foot to the right of me, a slender loophole in the wall. Swinging myself in, I found it was the aperture of a narrow horizontal tunnel in which I could lie down and rest. It was not too soon. My arms ached, my back was cramped, and I was trembling with the prolonged terror of a fall. Besides this, the unbroken darkness had had a distressing effect upon my eyes. The air was full of the throb and hum of machinery pumping air down the shaft.
“我不知道自己躺了多久。迷迷糊糊感到一只柔软的手在摸我的脸，才惊醒了过来。黑暗中，我一下子站起来，抓出我的火柴，急忙擦亮一根。我看到三个白色的动物，弯着腰，和我在上面废墟那里看到的那只很像。看到火光，他们急忙后退。由于长期生活在这样伸手不见五指的黑暗中，他们的眼睛出奇的大，而且极为敏感，就像深海鱼的两个瞳孔那样，而且它们反射光线的方式也一样。我毫不怀疑他们在这黑得不见一丝光的地方也能看见我，而且除了刚才火柴的光亮，他们似乎一点也不怕我。但是，我刚划亮一根火柴想看清楚他们时，他们就仓皇逃走了，消失在黑暗中的阴沟和地道里。从这些阴沟和地道中，我看到他们的眼睛瞪着我，目光极为奇怪。 ‘I do not know how long I lay. I was roused by a soft hand touching my face. Starting up in the darkness I snatched at my matches and, hastily striking one, I saw three stooping white creatures similar to the one I had seen above ground in the ruin, hastily retreating before the light. Living, as they did, in what appeared to me impenetrable darkness, their eyes were abnormally large and sensitive, just as are the pupils of the abysmal fishes, and they reflected the light in the same way. I have no doubt they could see me in that rayless obscurity, and they did not seem to have any fear of me apart from the light. But, so soon as I struck a match in order to see them, they fled incontinently, vanishing into dark gutters and tunnels, from which their eyes glared at me in the strangest fashion.
“我试着喊叫他们，但是他们的语言明显不同于上面世界。于是我孤立无援，就只好靠自己了，即使到了那个时候我也还有探险前逃跑的想法。但是我对自己说：‘你已经闯进虎穴了。’我摸索着沿地道向前走，耳边机器的隆隆声更响了。过了一会儿，两边的墙壁消失了，我来到一片开阔的空地。我又划亮一根火柴，原来我置身于一个拱形的洞穴中，洞里很深，一片漆黑，我的火柴也照不到尽头。我所看到的仅是火柴所照亮的一点范围。 ‘I tried to call to them, but the language they had was apparently different from that of the Over-world people; so that I was left to my own unaided efforts, and the thought of flight before exploration was even then in my mind. But I said to myself, “You are in for it now,” and, feeling my way along the tunnel, I found the noise of machinery grow louder. Presently the walls fell away from me, and I came to a large open space, and striking another match, saw that I had entered a vast arched cavern, which stretched into utter darkness beyond the range of my light. The view I had of it was as much as one could see in the burning of a match.
“我的记忆一定有些模糊。昏暗中冒出几个像大机器一样的东西，在地上投下奇怪的阴影。我隐约看到几个像鬼怪一样的莫洛克斯人被亮光吓得躲在那阴影里。顺便说一下，那个地方非常闷热压抑，空气中微微有种刚刚流出的鲜血的气味。中间某个地方有一张白色金属做的小桌子，上面摆着的像是一餐饭。不管怎样，莫洛克斯人竟然是食肉动物！即使那个时候，我记得自己还纳闷还有什么仍旧存活的大型动物能提供给他们这样一块红色的大腿肉。一切都很模糊：浓重的气味，呆板的庞然大物，还有潜伏在阴影中令人厌恶的身影，他们只等着周围陷入黑暗时再向我袭来！接着火柴燃尽了，烧到了我的手指，落在地上，黑暗中就只看到一点红色的火星在地上动弹了几下。 ‘Necessarily my memory is vague. Great shapes like big machines rose out of the dimness, and cast grotesque black shadows, in which dim spectral Morlocks sheltered from the glare. The place, by the by, was very stuffy and oppressive, and the faint halitus of freshly shed blood was in the air. Some way down the central vista was a little table of white metal, laid with what seemed a meal. The Morlocks at any rate were carnivorous! Even at the time, I remember wondering what large animal could have survived to furnish the red joint I saw. It was all very indistinct: the heavy smell, the big unmeaning shapes, the obscene figures lurking in the shadows, and only waiting for the darkness to come at me again! Then the match burned down, and stung my fingers, and fell, a wriggling red spot in the blackness.
“我一直在想，踏上这样一个探险之旅，自己带的装备真是少之又少。当我启动时光机器准备发出的时候，我荒谬地以为未来世界的人们会在各种装备水平上绝对超过我们。我来到这里既没有带武器，也没有带药品，连一支香烟也没有带——有些时候我特别想抽一支，甚至连火柴我也没有带多少。我要是想到带一个柯达相机就好了！我可以一下子就把刚才瞥到的一幕拍下来，等有空的时候再慢慢研究。但是，事实是，我站在那里，手无寸铁，只有大自然赋予我的武器和力量——我的双手、双脚，还有牙齿，外加剩下的四根安全火柴。 ‘I have thought since how particularly ill-equipped I was for such an experience. When I had started with the Time Machine, I had started with the absurd assumption that the men of the Future would certainly be infinitely ahead of ourselves in all their appliances. I had come without arms, without medicine, without anything to smoke—at times I missed tobacco frightfully—even without enough matches. If only I had thought of a Kodak! I could have flashed that glimpse of the Underworld in a second, and examined it at leisure. But, as it was, I stood there with only the weapons and the powers that Nature had endowed me with—hands, feet, and teeth; these, and four safety-matches that still remained to me.
“黑暗中，我不敢再往前走到那些机器之间。刚才那根火柴快燃尽时，我才发现自己带的火柴已经快用光了。直到那个时候，我才意识到自己应该省着点用。差不多有半盒都被我浪费掉，用来给上面世界的人们制造一点惊奇。对他们来说，火是个新鲜物。刚才说过，现在我就剩四根火柴了。黑暗中，我站在那，感到有只手在摸我的手，细长的手指在我的脸上抚摸，还有一股奇特难闻的气味。我周围应该有一群那些可怕的小东西，我似乎听到了他们的呼吸声。我感到有人在轻轻地从我手中拿走那盒火柴，其他一些人用手在背后拽着我的衣服。被这些看不见的东西这样玩弄，那种感觉让我厌恶得难以言表。黑暗中，我恍然大悟，意识到自己对他们的思考和行为方式一无所知。我尽可能大声地冲他们喊。他们吓了一跳，躲到一边，接着我感到他们又朝我走来。他们更加放肆地抓着我，用奇怪的声音互相低语。我浑身剧烈地颤抖，再次冲他们叫喊，声音相当刺耳。这一次他们没怎么受到惊吓，还发出奇怪的笑声，又冲我走来。我承认我怕得要命。我决定再划一根火柴，借着火光逃走。于是我擦亮火柴，并且从口袋中掏出一个纸片让它多燃烧一会儿。我成功退回到刚才那个狭窄的地道中。但是我刚一到那，我的火就被吹灭了。黑暗中，我听到莫洛克斯人在后面追赶过来，脚步沙沙作响，像是风刮过树叶的声音。他们啪嗒啪嗒的跑步声，像雨点落在地面上一样。 ‘I was afraid to push my way in among all this machinery in the dark, and it was only with my last glimpse of light I discovered that my store of matches had run low. It had never occurred to me until that moment that there was any need to economize them, and I had wasted almost half the box in astonishing the Upper-worlders, to whom fire was a novelty. Now, as I say, I had four left, and while I stood in the dark, a hand touched mine, lank fingers came feeling over my face, and I was sensible of a peculiar unpleasant odour. I fancied I heard the breathing of a crowd of those dreadful little beings about me. I felt the box of matches in my hand being gently disengaged, and other hands behind me plucking at my clothing. The sense of these unseen creatures examining me was indescribably unpleasant. The sudden realization of my ignorance of their ways of thinking and doing came home to me very vividly in the darkness. I shouted at them as loudly as I could. They started away, and then I could feel them approaching me again. They clutched at me more boldly, whispering odd sounds to each other. I shivered violently, and shouted again rather discordantly. This time they were not so seriously alarmed, and they made a queer laughing noise as they came back at me. I will confess I was horribly frightened. I determined to strike another match and escape under the protection of its glare. I did so, and eking out the flicker with a scrap of paper from my pocket, I made good my retreat to the narrow tunnel. But I had scarce entered this when my light was blown out and in the blackness I could hear the Morlocks rustling like wind among leaves, and pattering like the rain, as they hurried after me.
“不一会儿，我就被几双手抓住。不用说，他们是想把我拉回去。我又擦亮一根火柴，在他们面前挥动，照得他们眼晕。你几乎想不到他们长得有多恶心，人鬼不如：他们面色苍白，没有下巴，眼睛硕大，粉中带灰，而且没有长眼睑。他们就瞪着这样一双眼睛茫然困惑地看着我。但是我向你们保证，我没有停留下来仔细看。我接着撤逃，第二根火柴熄灭了，我擦亮第三根火柴。等第三根火柴快燃尽的时候，我刚好到达那个洞口的边缘。我躺在那里，下面抽气的那个机器砰砰的声音让我头晕。然后，我伸手在旁边摸着井壁突出的扶手，正摸索着，他们在后面抓住了我的脚，向后猛拽。我点燃最后一根火柴……它很快就熄灭了。但是，现在我一只手已经抓住了向上爬的横杆，我就用脚使劲踢，终于挣脱了那些莫洛克斯人。我迅速沿着井壁往上爬，身后他们停在那里眨巴着眼睛向上盯着我看。只有一个可恶的家伙追了我一段，还差点把我一只靴子夺了去当战利品。 ‘In a moment I was clutched by several hands, and there was no mistaking that they were trying to haul me back. I struck another light, and waved it in their dazzled faces. You can scarce imagine how nauseatingly inhuman they looked—those pale, chinless faces and great, lidless, pinkish-grey eyes!—as they stared in their blindness and bewilderment. But I did not stay to look, I promise you: I retreated again, and when my second match had ended, I struck my third. It had almost burned through when I reached the opening into the shaft. I lay down on the edge, for the throb of the great pump below made me giddy. Then I felt sideways for the projecting hooks, and, as I did so, my feet were grasped from behind, and I was violently tugged backward. I lit my last match ... and it incontinently went out. But I had my hand on the climbing bars now, and, kicking violently, I disengaged myself from the clutches of the Morlocks and was speedily clambering up the shaft, while they stayed peering and blinking up at me: all but one little wretch who followed me for some way, and wellnigh secured my boot as a trophy.
那井道似乎总也爬不到头。到最后二三十英尺的时侯，我感到恶心得要命。我的手十分吃力地抓着横杆。最后几码，我和这种软弱无力进行了一场可怕的斗争，拼命坚持不让自己昏过去。有好几次，我感到头晕眼花，跌落的感觉一次次向我袭来。然而，最终，我也不知怎么地翻过了井口，跌跌撞撞地走出那片废墟，来到了耀眼的阳光下。我栽倒在地上，闻着泥土的味道，感觉都是那么香甜清新。后来，我记得威娜在我的双手和耳朵上亲吻，还听到其他几个埃洛伊人说话的声音。这之后有一段时间，我失去了知觉。” ‘That climb seemed interminable to me. With the last twenty or thirty feet of it a deadly nausea came upon me. I had the greatest difficulty in keeping my hold. The last few yards was a frightful struggle against this faintness. Several times my head swam, and I felt all the sensations of falling. At last, however, I got over the well-mouth somehow, and staggered out of the ruin into the blinding sunlight. I fell upon my face. Even the soil smelt sweet and clean. Then I remember Weena kissing my hands and ears, and the voices of others among the Eloi. Then, for a time, I was insensible.’
第七章 CHAPTER VII
“现在，我的境况似乎比以前更糟糕了，的确是这样。到现在为止，除了丢了时光机器那天晚上痛苦万分，我心里曾一直怀有最终逃跑的希望，但如今，这些新发现动摇了我的这一希望。这之前，我一直以为自己是被那些小家伙孩子般的天真淳朴所牵绊，被某种未知的力量所阻碍，这力量我只有先弄明白才能战胜，但是我又发现，莫洛克斯人令人作呕的特性里还带有某种野蛮恶毒的成分。我本能地憎恶他们。之前，我感觉自己好比是一个人掉进了深坑之中，我关心的是这个坑和如何逃出这个坑。现在，我觉得自己像是一头陷阱中的困兽，而敌人很快将至。 ‘Now, indeed, I seemed in a worse case than before. Hitherto, except during my night’s anguish at the loss of the Time Machine, I had felt a sustaining hope of ultimate escape, but that hope was staggered by these new discoveries. Hitherto I had merely thought myself impeded by the childish simplicity of the little people, and by some unknown forces which I had only to understand to overcome; but there was anal together new element in the sickening quality of the Morlocks—a something inhuman and malign. Instinctively I loathed them. Before, I had felt as a man might feel who had fallen into a pit: my concern was with the pit and how to get out of it. Now I felt like a beast in a trap, whose enemy would come upon him soon.
“我担心的敌人可能会让你们大感意外，它就是新月时的‘黑夜’。威娜和我说过一些有关‘黑夜’的话，让我总想着这件事，虽然一开始听不懂她的话。现在，不难猜测这即将到来的‘黑夜’可能意味着什么。月亮在渐渐亏缺，黑夜持续的时间一天比一天长。现在，我至少略微理解了上面世界的人们对黑暗的恐惧。我感到有些困惑的是，莫洛克斯人在暗淡的新月下究竟会做出什么邪恶的勾当。现在我非常肯定自己的第二个假想是完全错误的。地上世界的人们也许曾经是养尊处优的贵族，而莫洛克斯人则是他们机械呆板的仆佣，但是那早已成为历史。人类进化出来的这两个种族之间正在或已经形成一种全新的关系。埃洛伊人就像加洛林王朝的国王一样，只是外表光鲜，实则败落。他们仍勉强统治着这个世界，因为无数代莫洛克斯人一直以来的地下生活最终让他们难以忍受阳光照耀的地面。据我推断，莫洛克斯人给地上世界的人们制作衣服，并且维持他们的日常需求，这也许是他们长期为仆残留的习惯。他们这一做法就像马站在那里会习惯地用蹄子刨地，或者就像一个人喜欢以猎杀动物来取乐一样。因为这一需求虽然存于久远，早已消失，但却已然让他们内化于心了。但是，很明显，旧有的秩序已经部分被逆转。复仇女神正悄悄向那些精致柔弱的人们逼近。很久很久之前，几千代以前，人类把他的同胞强行逐出了舒适的光明世界。而现在，昔日的兄弟卷土重来了，而且跟以前大不一样！埃洛伊人已经开始重新温习一堂旧课。他们又渐渐熟识了恐惧。突然，我记起在地下世界时看到的肉块。脑海中怎么会浮现这个，似乎有些奇怪。它可以说不是我的思绪勾起的记忆，而是像外部世界提出的一个问题一样闯入了我的脑海。我试着回忆那肉的样子。我有一种模糊的似曾相识的感觉，但是一时又说不出它到底是什么。 ‘The enemy I dreaded may surprise you. It was the darkness of the new moon. Weena had put this into my head by some at first incomprehensible remarks about the Dark Nights. It was not now such a very difficult problem to guess what the coming Dark Nights might mean. The moon was on the wane: each night there was a longer interval of darkness. And I now understood to some slight degree at least the reason of the fear of the little Upper-world people for the dark. I wondered vaguely what foul villainy it might be that the Morlocks did under the new moon. I felt pretty sure now that my second hypothesis was all wrong. The Upper-world people might once have been the favoured aristocracy, and the Morlocks their mechanical servants: but that had long since passed away. The two species that had resulted from the evolution of man were sliding down towards, or had already arrived at, an altogether new relationship. The Eloi, like theCarolingian1 kings, had decayed to a mere beautiful futility. They still possessed the earth on sufferance: since the Morlocks, subterranean for innumerable generations, had come at last to find the daylit surface intolerable. And the Morlocks made their garments, I inferred, and maintained them in their habitual needs, perhaps through the survival of an old habit of service. They did it as a standing horse paws with his foot, or as a man enjoys killing animals in sport: because ancient and departed necessities had impressed it on the organism. But, clearly, the old order was already in part reversed. The Nemesis of the delicate ones was creeping on apace. Ages ago, thousands of generations ago, man had thrust his brother man out of the ease and the sunshine. And now that brother was coming back changed! Already the Eloi had begun to learn one old lesson anew. They were becoming reacquainted with fear. And suddenly there came into my head the memory of the meat I had seen in the Under-world. It seemed odd how it floated into my mind: not stirred up as it were by the current of my meditations, but coming in almost like a question from outside. I tried to recall the form of it. I had a vague sense of something familiar, but I could not tell what it was at the time.
“然而，不管这些小人儿在面对他们神秘的恐惧时有多么无助，我跟他们有本质上的不同。我来自我们这个时代，来自人类成熟的全盛时期，恐惧不会让我们瘫痪无力，神秘已经失去了它的恐怖效应。我至少会保护自己。我决定立刻行动，自制一些武器，并建造一个可以睡觉的堡垒。当我意识到自己每晚都是那样睡着，对那些怪东西毫不设防，立刻没了安全感。有了那样一个安身之处当我的根据地，面对这个陌生的世界我就会稍微找回一些信心。我发现，在没有确保我的床铺完全安全，不受他们的威胁之前，我再也无法安心入睡。想到他们可能早已经将我仔细研究了一番，我不禁吓得发抖。 ‘Still, however helpless the little people in the presence of their mysterious fear, I was differently constituted. I came out of this age of ours, this ripe prime of the human race, when fear does not paralyse and mystery has lost its terrors. I at least would defend myself. Without further delay I determined to make myself arms and a fastness where I might sleep. With that refuge as a base, I could face this strange world with some of that confidence I had lost in realizing to what creatures night by night I lay exposed. I felt I could never sleep again until my bed was secure from them. I shuddered with horror to think how they must already have examined me.
“下午，我沿着泰晤士河谷闲逛，发现没有什么地方让我感觉是难以接近的。所有这些建筑和树木对于身手灵敏的莫洛克斯人来说似乎没什么难度，从莫洛克斯人惯常爬的井壁来看，一定是这样的。这时，我又回想起那个青瓷宫殿高高的尖石顶和光亮的墙壁。傍晚的时候，我带着威娜，把她像小孩一样放在肩上，朝西南方向的山上走去。我当时估计那距离大概有七八英里，但实际上肯定快十八英里了。我第一次看到那个地方是在一个潮湿的午后，因此这距离当时看起来比实际上要近一些。此外，我有一只鞋的鞋跟松动了，一个钉子快扎穿鞋底了——这双鞋是我之前在室内穿的一双旧鞋，很舒适——所以，我走路一瘸一拐的。当我看到那个宫殿的时候，太阳早已经落下去了，淡黄的天空映衬出那个宫殿黑色的轮廓。 ‘I wandered during the afternoon along the valley of the Thames, but found nothing that commended itself to my mind as inaccessible. All the buildings and trees seemed easily practicable to such dexterous climbers as the Morlocks, to judge by their wells, must be. Then the tall pinnacles of the Palace of Green Porcelain and the polished gleam of its walls came back to my memory; and in the evening, taking Weena like a child upon my shoulder, I went up the hills towards the south-west. The distance, I had reckoned, was seven or eight miles, but it must have been nearer eighteen. I had first seen the place on a moist afternoon when distances are deceptively diminished. In addition, the heel of one of my shoes was loose, and a nail was working through the sole—they were comfortable old shoes I wore about indoors—so that I was lame. And it was already long past sunset when I came in sight of the palace, silhouetted black against the pale yellow of the sky.
“我刚开始把威娜扛在肩上时，她兴高采烈。但是过了一会儿，她让我把她放下来，开始在我身旁跑，她忽而飞快地跑到我右边，忽而又奔向左边，摘几朵鲜花塞进我的口袋。我的两个口袋总让她困惑不已，但最后她得出的结论是，它们是一种不同寻常的花瓶，是用来插花装饰的。至少，她是把它们当花瓶用的。这个提醒了我！在换外套的时候我发现……” ‘Weena had been hugely delighted when I began to carry her, but after a while she desired me to let her down, and ran along by the side of me, occasionally darting off on either hand to pick flowers to stick in my pockets. My pockets had always puzzled Weena, but at the last she had concluded that they were an eccentric kind of vase for floral decoration. At least she utilized them for that purpose. And that reminds me! In changing my jacket I found...’
说到这里，时光旅行者停顿了一下，把手插进口袋，静静地把两朵枯萎的花摆在小桌子上，那花看着有点像硕大的白色锦葵。接着他继续自己的讲述。 The Time Traveller paused, put his hand into his pocket, and silently placed two withered flowers, not unlike very large white mallows, upon the little table. Then he resumed his narrative.
“当夜晚的寂静悄悄降临的时候，我们爬过一座山头向温布尔登的方向走去。威娜感到累了，想回到那个灰色的石头房子里。但是我指给她看远处那个青瓷宫殿的尖顶，设法使她明白我们会在那里找个躲避之处，躲过她对黑夜的恐惧。你们知道黄昏之前那种万籁俱寂的情景吧？连微风都像凝滞在树林间一般。我总感觉傍晚的宁静中有种期待的味道。天空晴朗，遥远而又空旷，只是天际的尽头还残留着几道落日的余晖。哦，那个晚上的期待中却夹杂着我的恐惧。在寂静的黑暗中，我的感官似乎异常敏锐起来。我似乎都能感到脚下大地已被挖空，我真的几乎能透过地面看到莫洛克斯人在他们的蚁穴中四处窜动，等待黑暗的到来。我激动地想象着他们会把我的擅自闯入看作是对他们的宣战。那他们为什么要拿走我的时光机器呢？ ‘As the hush of evening crept over the world and we proceeded over the hillcrest towards Wimbledon2, Weena grew tired and wanted to return to the house of grey stone. But I pointed out the distant pinnacles of the Palace of Green Porcelain to her, and contrived to make her understand that we were seeking a refuge there from her fear. You know that great pause that comes upon things before the dusk? Even the breeze stops in the trees. Tome there is always an air of expectation about that evening stillness. The sky was clear, remote, and empty save for a few horizontal bars far down in the sunset. Well, that night the expectation took the colour of my fears. In that darkling calm my senses seemed preternaturally sharpened. I fancied I could even feel the hollowness of the ground beneath my feet: could, indeed, almost see through it the Morlocks on their ant-hill going hither and thither and waiting for the dark. In my excitement I fancied that they would receive my invasion of their burrows as a declaration of war. And why had they taken my Time Machine?
“我们在一片寂静之中继续往前走，黄昏渐变为黑夜。远处晴朗的蓝天渐渐暗淡，星星一个接一个地闪现在天空中。大地变得模糊起来，树木也成了一个个黑影。威娜越发感到害怕和疲倦。我抱着她，跟她讲话，轻轻抚摸着她。天越来越黑，她用胳膊搂着我的脖子，闭上眼睛，把脸紧紧地贴在我的肩膀上。就这样，我们走下一个长长的山坡来到一个山谷中，眼前什么也看不清楚，我差点走进一条小河之中。我趟水过河，来到对岸的山谷往上走，经过了很多沉睡的房子，还有一尊雕像——一个半人半羊的农牧神像，或者类似的形象，只是没有头。这儿还有阿拉伯橡胶树。到目前为止，我还没有看到任何莫洛克斯人的影子，但是这会儿天才刚黑，残月出来之前更为黑暗的几个小时还没到呢。 ‘So we went on in the quiet, and the twilight deepened into night. The clear blue of the distance faded, and one star after another came out. The ground grew dim and the trees black. Weena’s fears and her fatigue grew upon her. I took her in my arms and talked to her and caressed her. Then, as the darkness grew deeper, she put her arms round my neck, and, closing her eyes, tightly pressed her face against my shoulder. So we went down a long slope into a valley, and there in the dimness I almost walked into a little river. This I waded, and went up the opposite side of the valley, past a number of sleeping houses, and by a statue—a Faun3, or some such figure, minus the head. Here too were acacias. So far I had seen nothing of the Morlocks, but it was yet early in the night, and the darker hours before the old moon rose were still to come.
“我看到下一座山的山顶覆盖着一片茂密的树林，黑漆漆一片，我迟疑了一下。这树林很大，不管是往左还是往右都看不到边。我感到累了，尤其是双脚酸疼得厉害，于是我停下脚步，把威娜轻轻从肩上放下来，坐在草坪上。我再也看不见那个青瓷宫殿，我怀疑自己是不是迷失了方向。我看着那片茂密的树林，心想着可能会有什么隐藏其中。那密密层层的树枝会把人遮挡得连天上的星星都看不到。即使这里没有任何其他什么潜在危险——我可不会放松自己对这一危险的警惕——也可能会被树根绊倒或是撞在树干上。 ‘From the brow of the next hill I saw a thick wood spreading wide and black before me. I hesitated at this. I could see no end to it, either to the right or the left. Feeling tired—my feet, in particular, were very sore—I carefully lowered Weena from my shoulder as I halted, and sat down upon the turf. I could no longer see the Palace of Green Porcelain, and I was in doubt of my direction. I looked into the thickness of the wood and thought of what it might hide. Under that dense tangle of branches one would be out of sight of the stars. Even were there no other lurking danger—a danger I did not care to let my imagination loose upon—there would still be all the roots to stumble over and the tree-boles to strike against.
“一天的紧张不安之后，我也很累了。因此，我决定不管自己的处境，就在这毫无遮蔽的山上过一晚。 ‘I was very tired, too, after the excitements of the day; so I decided that I would not face it, but would pass the night upon the open hill.
“看到威娜睡得正香，我很高兴。我小心地用外套给她盖好，在她旁边坐下，等着月亮出来。山坡上一片荒寂，但是黑暗的树林中不时有几个活物在那边一阵阵骚动，打破了夜的宁静。我头顶上群星闪耀，这是一个晴朗的夜晚。星星在空中一闪一闪的，给我一种友好舒适的感觉。那些昔日的星座都已从天空中消失了，它们经过缓慢的移动早已被重新排列成陌生的组群，但是这种变动在人一生的百年之中是难以察觉的。不过，银河看起来似乎还跟过去一样，还是以往那个星团汇成的破碎光带。往南（我判断是这个方向）有一颗红色的星星，非常明亮，我从来没有见过。它比我们绿色的天狼星还要闪亮。在这些光芒闪烁的亮点中间，有一颗明亮的行星，它的星光温和而恒定，感觉就像是一位故友的脸庞。 ‘Weena, I was glad to find, was fast asleep. I carefully wrapped her in my jacket, and sat down beside her to wait for the moonrise. The hillside was quiet and deserted, but from the black of the wood there came now and then a stir of living things. Above me shone the stars, for the night was very clear. I felt a certain sense of friendly comfort in their twinkling. All the old constellations had gone from the sky, however: that slow movement which is imperceptible in a hundred human lifetimes, had long since rearranged them in unfamiliar groupings. But the Milky Way, it seemed to me, was still the same tattered streamer of star-dust as of yore. Southward (as I judged it) was a very bright red star that was new to me; it was even more splendid than our own green Sirius. And amid all these scintillating points of light one bright planet shone kindly and steadily like the face of an old friend.
“看着这些星星，我突然感到自己的烦恼和所有俗世的牵绊都是多么微不足道。我想到它们的遥不可及，想到它们从无法知晓的过去一直到无从探知的未来都是这样缓慢而又永恒地运动着。我想到地球的轴极运动构成的大岁差周期。在我所穿越的这些年里，那样悄无声息地绕转进动只发生了四十次。在这些为数不多的旋转过程中，所有的活动，所有的传统，所有复杂的机构组织，所有的国家、语言、文学，各种志向抱负，甚至是我仅存记忆中所熟知的人类都已经被一扫而空。取而代之的是这些已经忘记他们高贵血统的娇弱生物，还有那些让我恐惧的白色家伙。接着，我想到这两个群种之间一方对另一方莫大的恐惧，冷不丁打了一个惊颤。我第一次清楚地知道了我之前见过的可能是什么肉。但是，这实在是太可怕了！我看着睡在我身旁的小威娜，她白皙的脸庞在星光的照耀下也带着星星一样的光辉，我立刻不再去想那些。 ‘Looking at these stars suddenly dwarfed my own troubles and all the gravities of terrestrial life. I thought of their unfathomable distance, and the slow inevitable drift of their movements out of the unknown past into the unknown future. I thought of the great precessional cycle4 that the pole of the earth describes. Only forty times had that silent revolution occurred during all the years that I had traversed. And during these few revolutions all the activity, all the traditions, the complex organizations, the nations, languages, literatures, aspirations, even the mere memory of Man as I knew him, had been swept out of existence. Instead were these frail creatures who had forgotten their high ancestry, and the white Things of which I went in terror. Then I thought of the great fear that was between the two species, and for the first time, with a sudden shiver, came the clear knowledge of what the meat I had seen might be. Yet it was too horrible! I looked at little Weena sleeping beside me, her face white and star like under the stars, and forthwith dismissed the thought.
