“在那个漫漫长夜里，我尽量不去想那些莫洛克斯人，想象自己可以在这全新的星座布局中找到原来一些星座的迹象，以此来打发时间。天空除了几片朦胧的云朵外，还是很晴朗的。我肯定自己时不时地打了几个盹儿。值夜的时间一点点过去，东边的天空出现了一抹微弱的光亮，就像没有颜色的火焰反射的光一样。一弯残月升上了天空，皎洁细弱，弯如满弓。就在它的后面，黎明的曙光慢慢溢满天空，盖过它。一开始还只是苍白的光亮，后来渐渐有了粉色，也变得温暖起来。没有一个莫洛克斯人靠近过我们。那天晚上，我在山上的确是一个也没有看到。新的一天又给了我自信，我几乎感觉自己真是没来由地担心害怕。我站起身，发现鞋跟松了的那只脚，脚后跟很疼，脚踝也肿了起来。于是我又坐了下来，脱掉鞋子，把它们扔到一边。 ‘Through that long night I held my mind off the Morlocks as well as I could, and whiled away the time by trying to fancy I could find signs of the old constellations in the new confusion. The sky kept very clear, except for a hazy cloud or so. No doubt I dozed at times. Then, as my vigil wore on, came a faintness in the eastward sky, like the reflection of some colourless fire, and the old moon rose, thin and peaked and white. And close behind, and overtaking it, and over flowing it, the dawn came, pale at first, and then growing pink and warm. No Morlocks had approached us. Indeed, I had seen none upon the hill that night. And in the confidence of renewed day it almost seemed to me that my fear had been unreasonable. I stood up and found my foot with the loose heel swollen at the ankle and painful under the heel; so I sat down again, took off my shoes, and flung them away.
“我唤醒威娜，然后一起朝那片树林走去。现在它看起来郁郁葱葱，景色怡人，不再像晚上那样黑漆一片，让人忘而却步。我们找到一些水果当作早餐。一会儿，我们又碰到其他一些娇小的家伙，他们在阳光下欢笑起舞，好像自然界根本没有黑夜这回事。而后我又想到之前看到的肉。现在，我很肯定那到底是什么肉，我从心底可怜这些在人类的滔滔洪流中仅存的最后一点孱弱的生命，像小溪一样潺潺流淌。很明显，在很久之前，人类衰败的某个时刻，莫洛克斯人的食物变得匮乏。他们可能以老鼠以及诸如此类的害虫为食。即使是现在，人类对食物也不如原来那么挑剔，吃的东西越来越多样化，食谱比任何一种猴子都要繁杂。人类对人肉本能的偏见也不是那么根深蒂固的。于是，这群人类野蛮的后代就……！我试着以科学的眼光去看待这件事情。毕竟，他们比我们三四千年以前的食肉祖先更没有人性，距离更遥远。而且原本把吃人这种事看作是种折磨的智力水平也已经消失了。我为什么还要自寻烦恼呢？这些埃洛伊人仅仅是被养肥的牲畜，莫洛克斯人像蚂蚁储粮一样把他们存留在那里，需要的时候就猎杀——可能还照料、饲养他们。而此刻威娜还在我身旁跳着舞呢！ ‘I awakened Weena, and we went down into the wood, now green and pleasant instead of black and forbidding. We found some fruit where with to break our fast. We soon met others of the dainty ones, laughing and dancing in the sunlight as though there was no such thing in nature as the night. And then I thought once more of the meat that I had seen. I felt assured now of what it was, and from the bottom of my heart I pitied this last feeble rill from the great flood of humanity. Clearly, at sometime in the long-ago of human decay the Morlocks’ food had run short. Possibly they had lived on rats and such-like vermin. Even now man is far less discriminating and exclusive in his food than he was—far less than any monkey. His prejudice against human flesh is no deep-seated instinct. And so these inhuman sons of men—! I tried to look at the thing in a scientific spirit. After all, they were less human and more remote than our cannibal ancestors of three or four thousand years ago. And the intelligence that would have made this state of things a torment had gone. Why should I trouble myself? These Eloi were mere fatted cattle, which the ant-like Morlocks preserved and preyed upon—probably saw to the breeding of. And there was Weena dancing at my side!
“然后，我试着驱散这正向我袭来的恐惧，把这一残酷的事实看作是人类的自私所遭受的严厉惩罚。人类心安理得地把自己的舒适和愉悦建立在同胞的辛苦劳作上，还标榜这样做是出于必要性，并以此为借口。现在，时机到了，人类也真正体会了这一必要性。我甚至试图模仿卡莱尔的风格讽刺这些可怜的没落贵族。但是，我是不可能有这种心态的。不管埃洛伊人的智力退化到怎样的水平，他们仍旧在很大程度上保留有人类的外形，不可能不引发我的同情，也必然使我与他们一起分担他们的恐惧，共同面对衰退的后果。 ‘Then I tried to preserve myself from the horror that was coming upon me, by regarding it as a rigorous punishment of human selfishness. Man had been content to live in ease and delight upon the labours of his fellow-man, had taken necessity as his watchword and excuse, and in the fullness of time necessity had come home to him. I even tried a Carlyle5-like scorn of this wretched aristocracy in decay. But this attitude of mind was impossible. However great their intellectual degradation, the Eloi had kept too much of the human form not to claim my sympathy, and to make me perforce a sharer in their degradation and their fear.
“当时，我并不十分明确自己应该走哪条路。我首先想到的是找一个安全的避身之处，并自制一些力所能及的金属或石头之类的武器，这一需求迫在眉睫。接下来，我希望能找到一些取火的工具，那样我就可以手举火把当作武器，因为我知道，对付莫洛克斯人，没有什么比火更有力的武器了。我还要想计策打开那个白色雕像下面的青铜门。我想到了古代攻城用的木槌。我相信如果我可以进去，带上一束火光照在我面前，我就能找到时光机器，然后逃走。莫洛克斯人不会把时光机器转移得太远，我还想象不出他们能有那么大的力量。至于威娜，我决定把她带回我们的时代。我脑中仔细考虑着这些计划，和威娜一起继续朝我设想将成为我们住处的那座建筑走去。” ‘I had at that time very vague ideas as to the course I should pursue. My first was to secure some safe place of refuge, and to make myself such arms of metal or stone as I could contrive. That necessity was immediate. In the next place, I hoped to procure some means of fire, so that I should have the weapon of a torch at hand, for nothing, I knew, would be more efficient against these Morlocks. Then I wanted to arrange some contrivance to break open the doors of bronze under the White Sphinx. I had in mind a battering ram. I had a persuasion that if I could enter those doors and carry a blaze of light before me I should discover the Time Machine and escape. I could not imagine the Morlocks were strong enough to move it far away. Weena I had resolved to bring with me to our own time. And turning such schemes over in my mind I pursued our way towards the building which my fancy had chosen as our dwelling.’
第八章 Chapter VIII
“大约中午的时候，我找到了那座青瓷宫殿，发现它已经无人居住，成了一片废墟。只看到窗户上还残留一些碎玻璃，建筑物正面那些大片的绿色装饰层已经从腐蚀的金属框架中掉落。它高高位于一个青草覆盖的丘陵之上，我进去之前朝东北方向看了一眼，惊奇地发现了一个巨大的河口，甚至可以说是一个小港。我判断那个地方曾经是旺兹沃思和巴特西的所在。接着我就想到海里的生物可能已经或是正在经历怎样的变迁，尽管我从来没有再进一步去思考这个问题。 ‘I found the Palace of Green Porcelain, when we approached it about noon, deserted and falling into ruin. Only ragged vestiges of glass remained in its windows, and great sheets of the green facing had fallen away from the corroded metallic framework. It lay very high upon a turfy down, and looking north-eastward before I entered it, I was surprised to see a large estuary, or even creek, where I judged Wandsworth1 and Battersea2 must once have been. I thought then—though I never followed up the thought—of what might have happened, or might be happening, to the living things in the sea.
“经过仔细查看，那座宫殿确实是用瓷器做的。在它正面刻着一些我看不懂的文字。我愚蠢地以为，也许威娜可以帮助我解释那些文字，结果却发现她脑子里根本连书写这一概念都没有。她给我的感觉似乎总比真正的她更近乎于人类，也许是因为她的感情更加富有人性。 ‘The material of the Palace proved on examination to be indeed porcelain, and along the face of it I saw an inscription in some unknown character. I thought, rather foolishly, that Weena might help me to interpret this, but I only learned that the bare idea of writing had never entered her head. She always seemed to me, I fancy, more human than she was, perhaps because her affection was so human.
“两扇大门敞开着，已经坏了。进到里面我们看到的不是通常的大厅，而是一个长长的走廊，两边有很多窗户可以采光。第一眼看到它让我想到了博物馆。地面是砖铺的，积了厚厚一层灰尘，走廊中陈列了各种各样的物品，也都盖着灰蒙蒙的一层尘土。接着，我看到大厅中央立着一个奇怪的东西，瘦骨嶙峋的，明显是一个大型动物骨架的下半部分。看到它倾斜的脚，我认出它是某种像大地懒一样已经灭绝的动物。头骨和上半部分的骨架陷在一旁厚厚的尘土之中。骨架有一块地方被从屋顶渗透下来的雨水侵蚀磨损。再往走廊里走，我看到一个巨大的雷龙骨架。我对这里是博物馆的猜想得到了证实。我朝走廊一侧走去，发现了一样东西，它看上去像是倾斜的架子。我拂去厚厚的灰尘，看到一些我们这个时代常见的玻璃展箱。但是从里面保存尚好的东西来看，这些玻璃箱肯定是密封的。 ‘Within the big valves of the door—which were open and broken—we found, instead of the customary hall, a long gallery lit by many side windows. At the first glance I was reminded of a museum. The tiled floor was thick with dust, and a remarkable array of miscellaneous objects was shrouded in the same grey covering. Then I perceived, standing strange and gaunt in the centre of the hall, what was clearly the lower part of a huge skeleton. I recognized by the oblique feet that it was some extinct creature after the fashion of the Megatherium. The skull and the upper bones lay beside it in the thick dust, and in one place, where rain-water had dropped through a leak in the roof, the thing itself had been worn away. Further in the gallery was the huge skeleton barrel of a Brontosaurus. My museum hypothesis was confirmed. Going towards the side I found what appeared to be sloping shelves, and clearing away the thick dust, I found the old familiar glass cases of our own time. But they must have been airtight to judge from the fair preservation of some of their contents.
“我们现在显然是站在日后南肯辛顿的遗址之中！这里明显是古生物区域，它一定曾有过极为壮观的化石陈列。尽管难以避免的腐化过程暂时得以避免，并且由于细菌和真菌的消亡而丧失了它百分之九十九的腐蚀力，但是这一过程还是必然会再次作用于这里的珍品，只是极为缓慢。这里到处都能发现那些小家伙的影子，看那些珍贵的化石就知道了，要么碎成了几块，要么是用绳子穿在芦苇上。有几个玻璃展箱被整体移动了，我判断可能是莫洛克斯人干的。这个地方很安静。厚厚的灰尘减弱了我们的脚步声。威娜一直在一个柜子的斜坡玻璃上滚海胆。不一会儿，她朝我走过来，我正凝视着四周，她默默地握住我的手，站在我身旁。 ‘Clearly we stood among the ruins of some latter-day South Kensington3! Here, apparently, was the Palaeontological Section, and a very splendid array of fossils it must have been, though the inevitable process of decay that had been staved off for a time, and had, through the extinction of bacteria and fungi, lost ninety-nine hundredths of its force, was nevertheless, with extreme sureness if with extreme slowness at work again upon all its treasures. Here and there I found traces of the little people in the shape of rare fossils broken to pieces or threaded in strings upon reeds. And the cases had in some instances been bodily removed—by the Morlocks as I judged. The place was very silent. The thick dust deadened our footsteps. Weena, who had been rolling a sea urchin down the sloping glass of a case, presently came, as I stared about me, and very quietly took my hand and stood beside me.
“一开始，我惊叹于眼前这个智慧时代的古迹，一点也没有想到它呈现出的种种可能性。甚至于我的头等大事——时光机器暂时也退居脑后了。 ‘And at first I was so much surprised by this ancient monument of an intellectual age, that I gave no thought to the possibilities it presented. Even my preoccupation about the Time Machine receded a little from my mind.
“从面积来看，这个青瓷宫殿绝不仅仅只有一个古生物展廊，或许还有历史展览馆，甚至可能还会有一个图书馆！对我来说，至少在目前的情况下，那些要比这些正在腐蚀的古代地质陈列品要有趣得多。我继续摸索，又看到一个展廊，这个要短一些，与第一个走廊横向交汇。这个走廊好像陈列的都是矿石，眼前出现的一块硫磺让我想到了火药。但是我找不到硝石，任何一种硝酸盐类物质都没看到。毫无疑问，它们在很久之前就已经溶解了。但是硫磺仍旧在我脑中挥之不去，我由它又想到了很多。至于第二个走廊里的其他陈列品，尽管总体上讲它们是我所看到的展品里保存得最完好的，但是我也不是什么矿物学专家，对它们都没什么兴趣。继续往前走，我来到了一个破败不堪的通道，与我第一次进的那个大厅平行。这里明显是自然历史展区，但是所有的东西都早已面貌全非。一些曾经是被制成标本的动物，现在只能看到一些皱巴巴的、发黑的残迹。曾经鲜活的动物现在只是罐子里的一具具干尸，还有几株植物，现在已经化作一堆棕色的灰烬，仅此而已！看到这些我觉得很遗憾，因为我原本是乐意去探索人类对动植物都做了哪些显著的调整，人类正是通过这些调整征服了生机勃勃的大自然。接着，我们来到了一个巨大的展室，但是光线却非常暗。它的地板从我进去的这一端开始略微往下倾斜。天花板上每隔一段距离挂着几个白色的球形灯，很多都破裂或是被打碎了，这些灯表明这里原先是采用人工照明的。到了这里，我感觉更合我的心意，因为出现在我左右两边的都是一些大型的机器，腐蚀得都很严重，很多还坏掉了，但还有一些仍然比较完好。我想要在它们中间逗留一会儿，你们知道我一看到机器就挪不动步，更何况这些机器带给我的困惑在很大程度上引起了我的兴趣，我只能凭空猜测它们是做什么用的。出于这个原因，我更加愿意驻足停留。我想如果我能解出这些谜题的话，就应该可以得到强大的力量，在对付莫洛克斯人时也许能派上用场。 ‘To judge from the size of the place, this Palace of Green Porcelain had a great deal more in it than a Gallery of Palaeontology; possibly historical galleries; it might be, even a library! To me, at least in my present circumstances, these would be vastly more interesting than this spectacle of old time geology in decay. Exploring, I found another short gallery running transversely to the first. This appeared to be devoted to minerals, and the sight of a block of sulphur set my mind running on gunpowder. But I could find no saltpeter; indeed, no nitrates of any kind. Doubtless they had deliquesced ages ago. Yet the sulphur hung in my mind, and set up a train of thinking. As for the rest of the contents of that gallery, though on the whole they were the best preserved of all I saw, I had little interest. I am no specialist in mineralogy, and I went on down a very ruinous aisle immediate presence of the Morlocks revived at that. I felt that I was wasting my time in the academic examination of machinery. I called to mind that it was already far advanced in the afternoon, and that I had still no weapon, no refuge, and no means of making a fire. And then down in the remote blackness of the gallery I heard a peculiar pattering, and the same odd noises I had heard down the well.
“突然，威娜紧紧靠在我身旁。那么突然，把我吓了一跳。如果不是她，我全然没有察觉展室的地板是倾斜的。我进来的那一段高出地面一大截，光线从几扇罕见的狭缝一样的窗户照进来。一直走下去，地面就和那些窗户相接了。走到最后会看到一个地洞，有点像伦敦房屋前面的‘采光井’，只在洞上方有一丝光亮。我慢慢地往前走着，还在苦想着这些机器，我一直太专注于想那些机器，都没有注意到往前走光线越来越暗，直到发现威娜愈发地紧张害怕，这才引起我的注意。接着我看到展室一直往下走那一头是一片黑暗。我犹豫了一下，环顾四周，发现地上没有那么多灰尘，也不是那么平整了。再往前朝着那片黑暗的方向，地上出现了很多窄小的脚印。看到那些脚印，我再次意识到莫洛克斯人随时会出现。我感到自己对机器的一番学术研究是在浪费时间。我意识到下午早已过去一大半了，而我还是没有任何武器，没有躲避的地方，也没有取火的工具。接着，在展室那片无尽黑暗的深处，我听到了一阵奇特的嗒嗒声，还有我在井下时听到的那种奇怪的嘈杂声。 ‘I took Weena’s hand. Then, struck with a sudden idea, I left her and turned to a machine from which projected a lever not unlike those in a signal-box. Clambering upon the stand, and grasping this lever in my hands, I put all my weight upon it sideways. Suddenly Weena, deserted in the central aisle, began to whimper. I had judged the strength of the lever pretty correctly, for it snapped after a minute’s strain, and I rejoined her with a mace in my hand more than sufficient, I judged, for any Morlock skull I might encounter. And I longed very much to kill a Morlock or so. Very inhuman, you may think, to want to go killing one’s own descendants! But it was impossible, somehow, to feel any humanity in the things. Only my disinclination to leave Weena, and a persuasion that if I began to slake my thirst for murder my Time Machine might suffer, restrained me from going straight down the gallery and killing the brutes I heard.
“我抓着威娜的手，随后突然想到一个主意。我放开她，转身跑向一架机器。那架机器有一个突出的杆，有点像信号楼上的那种。我爬上机器，双手抓住那根杆，用尽浑身力气把它往一边推。威娜一个人被丢在中间的通道，突然呜咽着哭了起来。那根杆的结实度我判断得很准确，因为在我用力推了一分钟后终于把它折断了。我又回到威娜身边，手中握着这根权杖，我断定有了它，遇到任何一个莫洛克斯人都可以应对。我十分渴望能亲手杀死一两个莫洛克斯人。你们可能会觉得想杀死自己的后代太不人道了！但是不知怎么的，你是不可能在那些东西身上觉出有什么人性的地方。我没有径直跑到展室尽头杀死我听到的那些野蛮人，只是因为不愿离开威娜，而且我相信如果为了图一时畅快杀掉他们，我的时光机器就可能会遭殃了。 ‘Well, mace in one hand and Weena in the other, I went out of that gallery and into another and still larger one, which at the first glance reminded me of a military chapel hung with tattered flags. The brown and charred rags that hung from the sides of it, I presently recognized as the decaying vestiges of books. They had long since dropped to pieces, and every semblance of print had left them. But here and there were warped boards and cracked metallic clasps that told the tale well enough. Had I been a literary man I might, perhaps, have moralized upon the futility of all ambition. But as it was, the thing that struck me with keenest force was the enormous waste of labour to which this sombre wilderness of rotting paper testified. At the time I will confess that I thought chiefly of the Philosophical Transactions4 and my own seventeen papers upon physical optics.
“这之后，我们爬上一段宽阔的楼梯，来到另一个展廊，这里也许曾经是工业化学展厅。我非常希望能在这里发现一些有用的东西。除了一端的房顶倒塌之外，这里保存得还很完好。我急切地把每一个还未破碎的展箱都看了一遍。终于，在这些密封得非常严实的箱子中，我发现其中一个里面有一盒火柴。我迫不及待地试了一下，它们还非常好用，甚至都没有受潮。我转向威娜，用她们的语言对她喊：‘跳舞吧！’因为现在我有了真正的武器，可以对付我们害怕的那些恐怖的家伙。于是，在那个废弃的博物馆里，我无比欢快地吹着口哨——《天国乐土》，踩着地上厚厚的灰尘，就像踏在柔软的地毯上一样，认真地跳起了我自己发明的复合舞。威娜看着我又唱又跳的，高兴极了。我一会儿是温和的康康舞，一会儿是踢踏舞，一会儿是长裙舞（在我的燕尾服能做到的限度内），一会儿又是我自己自创的舞姿。你们也知道，我天生就善于创造。 ‘Then, going up a broad staircase, we came to what may once have been a gallery of technical chemistry. And here I had not a little hope of useful discoveries. Except at one end where the roof had collapsed, this gallery was well preserved. I went eagerly to every unbroken case. And at last, in one of the really air-tight cases, I found a box of matches. Very eagerly I tried them. They were perfectly good. They were not even damp. I turned to Weena. “Dance,” I cried to her in her own tongue. For now I had a weapon indeed against the horrible creatures we feared. And so, in that derelict museum, upon the thick soft carpeting of dust, to Weena’s huge delight, I solemnly performed a kind of composite dance, whistling The Land of the Leal as cheerfully as I could. In part it was a modest Cancan5, in part a step dance, in part askirt-dance6 (so far as my tail-coat permitted), and in part original. For I am naturally inventive, as you know.
“现在，我仍然认为，这盒火柴历经不知多少年时光流转还完好地存留了下来，真是一件奇怪的事情。而对我来说，也是一件非常幸运的事情。但是，稀奇的是，我还找到一件更为不可思议的东西，那就是樟脑。我是在一个密封的广口瓶里发现的。我猜它可能是无意中被牢牢实实地密封起来的。一开始，我以为它是石蜡，于是就把玻璃瓶砸开了。但是，它散发出来的气味一闻就知道，肯定是樟脑，错不了的。万物消亡之中，这种挥发性物质也许经历了几十万年的时光，偶然得以存留下来。看到这块樟脑，我记起曾见到有人用箭石化石里的墨绘制的一幅乌贼墨画。那箭石一定是在数百万年之前死去并变成化石的。我正要把那块樟脑扔掉，但又想起来它是易燃物，烧起来有明亮的火光——它实际上是极好的蜡烛——于是，我就把它放进了口袋。但是，我没有找到炸药，也没有找到任何能破开那个青铜门的工具。目前为止我手中这根铁撬是我偶然发现的最有用的工具了。不过，离开那个展廊时我还是极为兴奋的。 ‘Now, I still think that for this box of matches to have escaped the wear of time for immemorial years was a most strange, as for me it was a most fortunate thing. Yet, oddly enough, I found a far unlikelier substance, and that was camphor. I found it in a sealed jar, that by chance, I suppose, had been really hermetically sealed. I fancied at first that it was paraffin wax, and smashed the glass accordingly. But the odour of camphor was unmistakable. In the universal decay this volatile substance had chanced to survive, perhaps through many thousands of centuries. It reminded me of a sepia painting I had once seen done from the ink of a fossil Belemnite7 that must have perished and become fossilized millions of years ago. I was about to throw it away, but I remembered that it was in flammable and burned with a good bright flame—was, in fact, an excellent candle—and I put it in my pocket. I found no explosives, however, nor any means of breaking down the bronze doors. As yet my iron crowbar was the most helpful thing I had chanced upon. Nevertheless I left that gallery greatly elated.
“我无法告诉你们那个漫长的下午发生的所有事情。我需要费很大的脑筋才能把我的探险经历井然有序地回忆起来。我记得有一个长长的走廊里面展示着一些生锈的武器，我还在那里犹豫不决，不知是该留着我手中的铁撬，还是选一个短柄小斧或是一把剑。可我同时拿不了两样，最后还是觉得我的铁棍是破门最好的工具。那里还有不少的枪支，有手枪和步枪。大部分都锈迹斑斑，但是还有很多是用某种陌生金属做的，还比较完好。但是原先可能陈列在那里的所有子弹或者火药都已经腐化成了尘土。我看到有一个角落被烧得焦黑，看上去还破碎凌乱。我想也许是展品之间发生了爆炸导致的。在另一处，我看到了一大片雕像——有波利尼西亚人、墨西哥人、希腊人、腓尼基人，我想应该涵盖了地球上所有的国家。在这里，我抑制不住冲动，把自己的名字写在了一个滑石怪物的鼻子上，这个来自南美洲的怪兽尤其吸引我。 ‘I cannot tell you all the story of that long afternoon. It would require a great effort of memory to recall my explorations in at all the proper order. I remember a long gallery of rusting stands of arms, and how I hesitated between my crowbar and a hatchet or a sword. I could not carry both, however, and my bar of iron promised best against the bronze gates. There were numbers of guns, pistols, and rifles. The most were masses of rust, but many were of some new metal, and still fairly sound. But any cartridges or powder there may once have been had rotted into dust. One corner I saw was charred and shattered; perhaps, I thought, by an explosion among the specimens. In another place was a vast array of idols—Polynesian, Mexican, Grecian, Phoenician, every country on earth I should think. And here, yielding to an irresistible impulse, I wrote my name upon the nose of a steatite monster from South America that particularly took my fancy.
“傍晚将至，我的兴趣也渐渐消退。我穿过一个又一个寂静的展厅，都是落满灰尘，往往破败不堪。那些展品有些仅仅只是一堆铁锈和褐煤，有些保存得好一些。我走到一个地方，突然发现自己旁边是一个锡矿模型，接着我发现在一个密封的玻璃箱内，有两个炸药筒！这一发现纯属偶然。我大喊：‘找到了！’然后惊喜地砸破玻璃。接着，我心生疑虑，迟疑了一下。我挑了侧边一个小展厅进行尝试。我静静地等了五分钟，十分钟，十五分钟，但是一直没有听到爆炸声。我从来没有感到过如此失望。当然了，它们都是仿造的，我应该早就猜到不可能把真的摆放在这里。我深信，如果它们不是样品的话，我早就不假思索地飞奔离去，把那个斯芬克斯雕像、青铜门，还有找回时光机器的希望（事实证明的确如此）统统都炸得无影无踪。 ‘As the evening drew on, my interest waned. I went through gallery after gallery, dusty, silent, often ruinous, the exhibits sometimes mere heaps of rust and lignite, sometimes fresher. In one place I suddenly found myself near the model of a tin-mine, and then by the merest accident I discovered, in an air-tight case, two dynamite cartridges! I shouted “Eureka!” and smashed the case with joy. Then came a doubt. I hesitated. Then, selecting a little side gallery, I made my essay. I never felt such a disappointment as I did in waiting five, ten, fifteen minutes for an explosion that never came. Of course the things were dummies, as I might have guessed from their presence. I really believe that had they not been so, I should have rushed off incontinently and blown Sphinx, bronze doors, and (as it proved) my chances of finding the Time Machine, all together into nonexistence.
“我想，在那之后我们就到了宫殿中一个露天的庭院。它上面盖有草皮，里面还有三棵果树。我们就在那休息了一下，恢复了些精神。快日落的时候，我开始思考我们现在的处境。夜幕渐渐降临，我还没有找到可以藏身的地方。但是现在，我已经不太担心这个问题了。我现在有了或许是对付莫洛克斯人最好的防备武器——我有火柴了！如果需要一束耀人的火焰，我口袋里还有樟脑。在我看来，似乎最好的办法就是在这个露天的地方过夜，生一堆火作保护。等到早上，就去拿回时光机器。对此，我目前手中用得上的就只有那根铁棍。但是现在，随着了解的情况渐渐多起来，我对那些青铜门的看法也不大相同。在此之前，我一直竭力避免用蛮力砸开它们，主要是因为门的另一边还是个谜。我从未觉得那门有多么坚固，希望我的铁棍多少还能胜任。” ‘It was after that, I think, that we came to a little open court within the palace. It was turfed, and had three fruit-trees. So we rested and refreshed ourselves. Towards sunset I began to consider our position. Night was creeping upon us, and my inaccessible hiding-place had still to be found. But that troubled me very little now. I had in my possession a thing that was, perhaps, the best of all defences against the Morlocks—I had matches! I had the camphor in my pocket, too, if a blaze were needed. It seemed to me that the best thing we could do would be to pass the night in the open, protected by a fire. In the morning there was the getting of the Time Machine. Towards that, as yet, I had only my iron mace. But now, with my growing knowledge, I felt very differently towards those bronze doors. Up to this, I had refrained from forcing them, largely because of the mystery on the other side. They had never impressed me as being very strong, and I hoped to find my bar of iron not altogether inadequate for the work.’
第九章 Chapter IX
“我们从宫殿里出来时，太阳还有一部分在地平线上。我决定第二天一早赶到白色雕像那里，并打算在黄昏之前穿过那片茂密的树林。上次来的时候，我被它挡在了路上。我计划在那天晚上尽快往前赶路，然后生一堆火，在火光的保护下睡觉。于是，一路走的时候，我看到有任何木棍或干草就都收集了起来。不多久，我的怀里就抱了满满一堆这些乱七八糟的东西。有了这些负重，我们的速度比我预想的要慢。此外，威娜感觉累了，我也开始犯困，因此我们还没走到那片树林，天就已经很黑了。走到山上这片灌木丛边缘时，眼前的黑暗让威娜害怕，她真想不再往前走了。但是我有一种奇怪的感觉，似乎灾难的脚步正在逼近。一定是这一想法警告了我，催促着我继续往前走。我已经两天一夜没有睡觉了，身上发热，焦躁不安。我感到睡意袭来，而莫洛克斯人也在向我袭来。 ‘We emerged from the palace while the sun was still in part above the horizon. I was determined to reach the White Sphinx early the next morning, and ere the dusk I purposed pushing through the woods that had stopped me on the previous journey. My plan was to go as far as possible that night, and then, building a fire, to sleep in the protection of its glare. Accordingly, as we went along I gathered any sticks or dried grass I saw, and presently had my arms full of such litter. Thus loaded, our progress was slower than I had anticipated, and besides Weena was tired. And I began to suffer from sleepiness too; so that it was full night before we reached the wood. Upon the shrubby hill of its edge Weena would have stopped, fearing the darkness before us; but a singular sense of impending calamity, that should indeed have served me as a warning, drove me onward. I had been without sleep for a night and two days, and I was feverish and irritable. I felt sleep coming upon me, and the Morlocks with it.
“我们正犹豫不决时，我看到身后黑漆漆的森林中，隐约有三个身影蜷伏在黑暗中。我们周围都是一些矮树丛和长得很高的草，他们暗中靠近让我感觉很不安全。我估计走到森林那头大概还有不到一英里的路。如果我们可以穿过它，走到那片光秃秃的山坡上，就有一个可以休息的地方了。我感觉那里总体上更安全一些。我想在我们穿过这片森林的时候，可以设法用我的火柴和樟脑照路。但是，很显然，如果我要划火柴的话，两只手就必须放下抱着的柴火。于是，我很不情愿地把柴火放了下来。接着，我想到如果把它点着的话，我们后面的那几位‘朋友’肯定会被吓到。后来我才发现这一行动既愚蠢又残暴，但是当时我觉得它可以巧妙地掩护我们撤逃。 ‘While we hesitated, among the black bushes behind us, and dim against their blackness, I saw three crouching figures. There was scrub and long grass all about us, and I did not feel safe from their insidious approach. The forest, I calculated, was rather less than a mile across. If we could get through it to the bare hill-side, there, as it seemed to me, was an altogether safer resting-place; I thought that with my matches and my camphor I could contrive to keep my path illuminated through the woods. Yet it was evident that if I was to flourish matches with my hands I should have to abandon my firewood; so, rather reluctantly, I put it down. And then it came into my head that I would amaze our friends behind by lighting it. I was to discover the atrocious folly of this proceeding, but it came to my mind as an ingenious move for covering our retreat.
“我不知道你们是否想过在一个没有人，气候又温和的地方，火是多么罕见的东西。太阳的热量即使被露珠聚在一点也很少能燃烧起来，而这种情况在更接近热带的地区有时候会发生。闪电可能会击中什么，把东西炸坏，变得焦黑，但很少能引起蔓延的大火。腐烂的植物发酵产生的热量偶尔可能会引起闷燃，但是也很少会冒出火苗。在这个堕落颓废的时代，取火的技术也早已在地球上被遗忘了。因此，火焰如红舌一般吞噬着那堆柴火，这对威娜来说绝对是个新奇的东西。 ‘I don’t know if you have ever thought what a rare thing f lame must be in the absence of man and in a temperate climate. The sun’s heat is rarely strong enough to burn, even when it is focused by dewdrops, as is sometimes the case in more tropical districts. Lightning may blast and blacken, but it rarely gives rise to widespread fire. Decaying vegetation may occasionally smoulder with the heat of its fermentation, but this rarely results in flame. In this decadence, too, the art of fire-making had been forgotten on the earth. The red tongues that went licking up my heap of wood were an altogether new and strange thing to Weena.
“她想跑过去玩火。我相信，如果不是我制止她的话，她就扑进火里了。我抓住她，任凭她怎么挣扎，带着她勇猛地一头扎进了树林。那堆火照亮了前面的一小段路。过了一会儿，透过密密麻麻的树枝，我回头看到那堆火将旁边的一些矮树丛也引燃了，火苗连成一线，正在向山上的野草蜿蜒爬行。看到眼前的景象，我大笑起来，然后转身继续往前走。前面很黑，威娜紧紧地靠着我，吓得直哆嗦，但是我的眼睛渐渐适应了黑暗，那点微微的光亮足以让我躲过那些树枝。头顶上完全是漆黑一片，只是在很遥远的地方，蓝天透过一丝缝隙照着我们到处走。我一根火柴也没有划，因为我的两只手都被占着。左胳膊抱着小威娜，右手拿着铁棒。 ‘She wanted to run to it and play with it. I believe she would have cast herself into it had I not restrained her. But I caught her up, and in spite of her struggles, plunged boldly before me into the wood. For a little way the glare of my fire lit the path. Looking back presently, I could see, through the crowded stems, that from my heap of sticks the blaze had spread to some bushes adjacent, and a curved line of fire was creeping up the grass of the hill. I laughed at that, and turned again to the dark trees before me. It was very black, and Weena clung to me convulsively, but there was still, as my eyes grew accustomed to the darkness, sufficient light for me to avoid the stems. Overhead it was simply black, except where a gap of remote blue sky shone down upon us here and there. I struck none of my matches because I had no hand free. Upon my left arm I carried my little one, in my right hand I had my iron bar.
“有一段路，我只听到脚下踩到小树枝时发出的断裂声，微风吹过时沙沙的响声，我自己的呼吸声，还有耳中血管的搏动声，除此之外再听不到别的声音。紧接着，我好像听到周围有嗒嗒的声音。我坚定脚步，继续往前走。那嗒嗒的声音越来越清晰，然后我又听到了那个奇怪的声音和嘈杂声，跟我在地下世界听到的一样。显然我周围有几个莫洛克斯人，他们正在向我逼近。果然，过了一小会儿，我感到有人扯我的外套，接着胳膊上也感觉有什么东西。威娜吓得浑身猛烈地颤抖，大气都不敢出一口。 ‘For some way I heard nothing but the crackling twigs under my feet, the faint rustle of the breeze above, and my own breathing and the throb of the blood-vessels in my ears. Then I seemed to know of a pattering about me. I pushed on grimly. The pattering grew more distinct, and then I caught the same queer sound and voices I had heard in the Under-world. There were evidently several of the Morlocks, and they were closing in upon me. Indeed, in another minute I felt a tug at my coat, then something at my arm. And Weena shivered violently, and became quite still.
“是时候点一根火柴了。但是那样的话，我必须先把威娜放下来。于是，我放下她，在口袋里摸着火柴，这时我感到膝盖附近一阵撕扯挣扎。听到莫洛克斯人发出那种奇怪的咕咕声，威娜则一点声音也没有。一些软软的小手也爬上我的外套和后背，甚至还摸我的脖子。接着，我划亮了火柴，火柴头嘶嘶作响。我手举着燃烧的火柴，看到树木间几个莫洛克斯人匆忙逃离的白色背影。我急忙从兜里拿出一块樟脑，准备火柴一旦快熄灭就把它点着。然后，我看了一眼威娜。她抓着我的脚，一动不动地趴在地上。我吃了一惊，赶紧蹲下来看她。她好像几乎都没呼吸了。我点燃那块樟脑，扔在地上。樟脑裂开来，火苗一下子大了起来，驱散了黑暗，逼得莫洛克斯人往后退。我跪下来，抱起威娜。身后的树林一片骚动，到处都是咕咕哝哝的讲话声，听起来好像有一大群家伙！ ‘It was time for a match. But to get one I must put her down. I did so, and, as I fumbled with my pocket, a struggle began in the darkness about my knees, perfectly silent on her part and with the same peculiar cooing sounds from the Morlocks. Soft little hands, too, were creeping over my coat and back, touching even my neck. Then the match scratched and fizzed. I held it flaring, and saw the white backs of the Morlocks in f light amid the trees. I hastily took a lump of camphor from my pocket, and prepared to light it as soon as the match should wane. Then I looked at Weena. She was lying clutching my feet and quite motionless, with her face to the ground. With a sudden fright I stooped to her. She seemed scarcely to breathe. I lit the block of camphor and flung it to the ground, and as it split and flared up and drove back the Morlocks and the shadows, I knelt down and lifted her. The wood behind seemed full of the stir and murmur of a great company!
“威娜好像晕过去了。我轻轻把她靠在肩上，站起来继续往前走，这时我意识到一个可怕的事实。在放下威娜点火柴的过程中，我转了好几次身，现在一点也不清楚该往哪个方向走。我只知道，自己或许是背对着青瓷殿的。我出了一身冷汗。必须赶快想出该怎么办。我决定生一堆火，就在这个地方停下来过夜。我把威娜放在有一块草皮覆盖的红玄武土上，她还是一动不动，第一块樟脑快熄灭了，我赶忙找来一些枯枝和树叶。黑暗中，我周围到处都是莫洛克斯人红宝石一样发光的眼睛。 ‘She seemed to have fainted. I put her carefully upon my shoulder and rose to push on, and then there came a horrible realization. In manoeuvring with my matches and Weena, I had turned myself about several times, and now I had not the faintest idea in what direction lay my path. For all I knew, I might be facing back towards the Palace of Green Porcelain. I found myself in a cold sweat. I had to think rapidly what to do. I determined to build a fire and encamp where we were. I put Weena, still motionless, down upon a turfy bole, and very hastily, as my first lump of camphor waned, I began collecting sticks and leaves. Here and there out of the darkness round me the Morlocks’ eyes shone like carbuncles.
“樟脑的火光摇曳了几下，熄灭了。我又擦着一根火柴，就在这时，两个正朝威娜靠近的白色身影慌忙逃开了。其中一个被光刺得眼睛什么都看不到，径直朝我冲过来，我一拳打在他身上，感到他的骨头嘎嘎作响。他发出一声痛苦的惨叫，跌跌撞撞地走了几步，栽倒在了地上。我又拿出一块樟脑点着，继续拾柴火。不一会儿，我发现我头顶上的一些树叶非常干燥，自从我驾驶时光机器来到这里，大概有一星期了，一滴雨都没有下过。因此，我不再从树林中四处寻找落下的小树枝，我开始向上一跃，抓住树枝往下拉。不一会儿，一堆干树枝混着嫩枝叶冒着浓烟就燃起来了，这样我就可以省下樟脑了。接着，我转向威娜，她正躺在铁棍旁边。我用尽各种方法想让她醒过来，但她就像死去了一样躺在那里。我甚至都不确定她是否还在呼吸。 ‘The camphor flickered and went out. I lit a match, and as I did so, two white forms that had been approaching Weena dashed hastily away. One was so blinded by the light that he came straight for me, and I felt his bones grind under the blow of my fist. He gave a whoop of dismay, staggered a little way, and fell down. I lit another piece of camphor, and went on gathering my bonfire. Presently I noticed how dry was some of the foliage above me, for since my arrival on the Time Machine, a matter of a week, no rain had fallen. So, instead of casting about among the trees for fallen twigs, I began leaping up and dragging down branches. Very soon I had a choking smoky fire of green wood and dry sticks, and could economize my camphor. Then I turned to where Weena lay beside my iron mace. I tried what I could to revive her, but she lay like one dead. I could not even satisfy myself whether or not she breathed.
“现在，篝火的浓烟朝我扑打过来，肯定是一下子令我感到了浑身沉重。而且，空气中还弥漫着樟脑燃烧的烟雾。我的火大概一个小时内不需要添柴。忙碌一通之后，我感到很疲倦，就坐了下来。树林里到处弥漫着低沉的声音，催人入眠，我也不明白那是什么声音。我好像只是打了个盹，可一睁眼却发现眼前一片黑暗，那些莫洛克斯人抓着我。我甩掉他们黏在我身上的手指，慌忙伸手到口袋里去找火柴盒，结果发现它不见了！接着他们又抓住我，把我团团围住。我立刻明白过来刚才发生了什么事情。我睡着了，那堆火也熄灭了，死亡的痛苦涌进我心底。森林里似乎到处弥漫着木头燃烧的味道。他们抓住了我的脖子、头发，还有胳膊，将我拽倒在地上。黑暗中，我躺在地上，感觉那些软乎乎的家伙聚拢在我身上，我难以描述那种感觉有多么恐怖。我感觉就像是落入了一个可怕的蜘蛛网中。我被制服，倒了下去。我感到有细小的牙齿在轻轻啃啮我的脖子。我翻了个身，这么一来，我的手碰到了我的铁棒，它给了我力量。我挣扎着爬起来，把那些老鼠一样的人从我身上甩开，然后猛一下举起铁棍，估摸着他们脸的方位，用力戳过去。我能感到几棍下去，他们就都血肉横飞了。于是我暂时摆脱了他们。 ‘Now, the smoke of the fire beat over towards me, and it must have made me heavy of a sudden. Moreover, the vapour of camphor was in the air. My fire would not need replenishing for an hour or so. I felt very weary after my exertion, and sat down. The wood, too, was full of a slumbrous murmur that I did not understand. I seemed just to nod and open my eyes. But all was dark, and the Morlocks had their hands upon me. Flinging off their clinging fingers I hastily felt in my pocket for the match-box, and—it had gone! Then they gripped and closed with me again. In a moment I knew what had happened. I had slept, and my fire had gone out, and the bitterness of death came over my soul. The forest seemed full of the smell of burning wood. I was caught by the neck, by the hair, by the arms, and pulled down. It was indescribably horrible in the darkness to feel all these soft creatures heaped upon me. I felt as if I was in a monstrous spider’s web. I was over powered, and went down. I felt little teeth nipping at my neck. I rolled over, and as I did so my hand came against my iron lever. It gave me strength. I struggled up, shaking the human rats from me, and, holding the bar short, I thrust where I judged their faces might be. I could feel the succulent giving of flesh and bone under my blows, and for a moment I was free.
“我感到一阵欣喜，艰苦的战斗似乎常常伴随着奇怪的狂喜。我知道我和威娜都将成为他们的盘中餐，但我决心让他们为此付出代价。我背靠一棵树站着，在我前面挥舞铁棍。整个树林都是他们骚乱和叫喊的声音。过了一会儿，他们叫喊得更尖了，动作也变迅速了，但是我一个也够不着。我站在那里凝视着黑暗。突然我感觉有了希望：要是莫洛克斯人害怕了会怎样呢？紧接着，奇怪的事情发生了。黑暗似乎渐渐变得明亮起来。朦胧中，我开始看到周围的莫洛克斯人——有三个被我打倒在脚下。随后，让我难以置信的是，我发现在我身后其他一些莫洛克斯人竟一个接着一个地都跑掉了。消失在前面的树林中。他们的后背看起来不再是白色，而是略带红色。我站在那里，惊得目瞪口呆。这时，我看到一个红色的小火星飘过树枝缝隙间的星光，消失了。我这才明白树林里木头燃烧的味道，之前低沉的声音都是怎么回事，现在那声音已经变成强风般的咆哮了，也明白了为什么会有红色的光，还有莫洛克斯人为什么突然都逃掉了。 ‘The strange exultation that so often seems to accompany hard fighting came upon me. I knew that both I and Weena were lost, but I determined to make the Morlocks pay for their meat. I stood with my back to a tree, swinging the iron bar before me. The whole wood was full of the stir and cries of them. A minute passed. Their voices seemed to rise to a higher pitch of excitement, and their movements grew faster. Yet none came within reach. I stood glaring at the blackness. Then suddenly came hope. What if the Morlocks were afraid? And close on the heels of that came a strange thing. The darkness seemed to grow luminous. Very dimly I began to see the Morlocks about me—three battered at my feet—and then I recognized, with incredulous surprise, that the others were running, in an incessant stream, as it seemed, from behind me, and away through the wood in front. And their backs seemed no longer white, but reddish. As I stood agape, I saw a little red spark go drifting across a gap of starlight between the branches, and vanish. And at that I understood the smell of burning wood, the slumbrous murmur that was growing now into a gusty roar, the red glow, and the Morlocks’ flight.
“我从树后面走出来，回头看。从近处黑乎乎的树干间隙中，我看到森林燃烧的火光，那是我第一次生起的火从后面追上来了。我借着火光开始找威娜，但是她不见了。身后大火燃烧的嘶嘶声，树枝的迸裂声，每棵青翠的树木燃烧时‘轰’的爆炸声，这一切让我来不及思考。我一手紧握着铁棍，沿着莫洛克斯人刚才离开的路线跑。大火追得很紧。有一次，火焰迅速地蔓到了我的右侧，围住了我，我只得赶紧向左边跑。但最终，我跑到了一小块空旷的地方。刚到那里，一个莫洛克斯人笨拙地朝我扑过来，经过我，径直跑进了大火中！ ‘Stepping out from behind my tree and looking back, I saw, through the black pillars of the nearer trees, the flames of the burning forest. It was my first fire coming after me. With that I looked for Weena, but she was gone. The hissing and crackling behind me, the explosive thud as each fresh tree burst into flame, left little time for reflection. My iron bar still gripped, I followed in the Morlocks’ path. It was a close race. Once the flames crept forward so swiftly on my right as I ran that I was outflanked and had to strike off to the left. But at last I emerged upon a small open space, and as I did so, a Morlock came blundering towards me, and past me, and went on straight into the fire!
“我想我现在即将看到的一幕会是那个未来世界最怪异可怕的事情。整块空地被大火照得亮如白昼。在空地中间，一棵烧焦的山楂树下，有一个小山丘或者说是一座古墓。空地那边是另一片燃烧的森林。黄色的火苗已经在树林里翻腾，把这块空地完全包围在一圈大火之中。山腰上有三四十个莫洛克斯人。熊熊燃烧的大火使他们眩晕，迷迷糊糊地四处踉跄，你碰我，我撞你。一开始我没有意识到他们什么也看不见。看到他们向我靠近，我怕得发狂，就用铁棍狠狠地砸他们，我打死了一个，另外还有几个被我打得一瘸一拐的。但是，在火红的天空下，当我看到有一个莫洛克人在山楂树下摸索着爬行，听到他们痛苦的呻吟，我确定他们在火光中完全陷入痛苦和无助的境地，于是我没有再去打他们。 ‘And now I was to see the most weird and horrible thing, I think, of all that I beheld in that future age. This whole space was as bright as day with the reflection of the fire. In the centre was a hillock or tumulus, surmounted by a scorched hawthorn. Beyond this was another arm of the burning forest, with yellow tongues already writhing from it, completely encircling the space with a fence of fire. Upon the hill-side were some thirty or forty Morlocks, dazzled by the light and heat, and blundering hither and thither against each other in their bewilderment. At first I did not realize their blindness, and struck furiously at them with my bar, in a frenzy of fear, as they approached me, killing one and crippling several more. But when I had watched the gestures of one of them groping under the hawthorn against the red sky, and heard their moans, I was assured of their absolute helplessness and misery in the glare, and I struck no more of them.
“但是，不时会有一个莫洛克斯人径直冲我奔过来，发出一声颤抖的惨叫，我急忙躲开。有一会儿，火焰稍微变弱了一些，我担心那些可鄙的家伙不久就能看见我。我正想着在他们能看见我之前，先杀掉几个，但是火势重又旺了起来，我就没有动手。我在小山坡上四处走，在他们中间躲闪穿行，寻找威娜的踪迹。但是威娜就是不见了。 ‘Yet every now and then one would come straight towards me, setting loose a quivering horror that made me quick to elude him. At one time the flames died down somewhat, and I feared the foul creatures would presently be able to see me. I was thinking of beginning the fight by killing some of them before this should happen; but the fire burst out again brightly, and I stayed my hand. I walked about the hill among them and avoided them, looking for some trace of Weena. But Weena was gone.
“最后，我坐在小丘顶上，看着眼前这群难以置信的怪东西。现在他们什么也看不见了，在那里到处摸索。火光扑到他们身上的时候，彼此发出怪异的声音。滚滚浓烟盘旋直上划过天空。那红色的穹顶间或有几处缝隙。透过那缝隙可以看到闪耀的小星星。它们看上去那么遥远，像是来自另一个宇宙。又有两三个莫洛克斯人踉跄着朝我过来，我几拳头下去把他们赶走了，打他们的时候我自己也浑身发抖。 ‘At last I sat down on the summit of the hillock, and watched this strange incredible company of blind things groping to and fro, and making uncanny noises to each other, as the glare of the fire beat on them. The coiling uprush of smoke streamed across the sky, and through the rare tatters of that red canopy, remote as though they belonged to another universe, shone the little stars. Two or three Morlocks came blundering into me, and I drove them off with blows of my fists, trembling as I did so.
“那晚多半时候，我都说服自己去相信这只不过是一场噩梦。我咬自己，放声尖叫，急切地想把自己弄醒。我双手捶地，站起来，又坐下，四处徘徊，然后再坐下。接着，我开始揉我的眼睛，请求上帝让我醒过来。有三次，我看到莫洛克斯人痛苦地缩着他们的头，冲进了火里。但是最终，火势逐渐变弱，一股股的黑烟在空中摇曳，树桩被烧得焦黑或成了白灰，那些家伙的数量也在不断减少。终于出现了一道黎明的白光，俯照这一切。 ‘For the most part of that night I was persuaded it was a nightmare. I bit myself and screamed in a passionate desire to awake. I beat the ground with my hands, and got up and sat down again, and wandered here and there, and again sat down. Then I would fall to rubbing my eyes and calling upon God to let me awake. Thrice I saw Morlocks put their heads down in a kind of agony and rush into the flames. But, at last, above the subsiding red of the fire, above the streaming masses of black smoke and the whitening and blackening tree stumps, and the diminishing numbers of these dim creatures, came the white light of the day.
“我又开始寻找威娜的踪影，但是哪里也找不到。显而易见，莫洛克斯人把那可怜的小东西丢在了森林里。我想它最终逃脱了似乎是注定的命运，我无法描述这样想让我感到有多么宽慰。想到这个，我差点按捺不住要去把那些无助、可憎的家伙一个个都杀光，但我还是克制住了。我之前提到过，那个小丘就像这片森林中的一座小岛。站在它的最顶部，透过朦胧的烟雾，我依稀可以认出青瓷殿，据此我就能确定白色斯芬克斯雕像的方位。还剩下几个该死的莫洛克斯人在四处逃窜呻吟，而我离开了。这时，天越来越亮，我用草把脚缠裹起来系住，跛着脚继续朝藏着时光机器的地方走去。一路经过冒着烟的灰烬，四周都是烧焦的树干。树干里面的火还没有熄灭，还在噼噼啪啪地烧着。我走得很慢，因为我的脚跛着，而且我几乎筋疲力尽了，另外小威娜可怕的死去也让我无比悲痛。威娜的死像是一个巨大的灾难压在我心头。现在，在这间熟悉的屋子里，它似乎更像是一个悲伤的梦，而不是真的失去了她。但是，那天早上我再次感到极其孤独——孤独得可怕！我开始想到自己这栋房子，想到坐在火炉边，想到你们其中的一些人，而伴随这些思念的是一种痛苦的渴望。 ‘I searched again for traces of Weena, but there were none. It was plain that they had left her poor little body in the forest. I cannot describe how it relieved me to think that it had escaped the awful fate to which it seemed destined. As I thought of that, I was almost moved to begin a massacre of the helpless abominations about me, but I contained myself. The hillock, as I have said, was a kind of island in the forest. From its summit I could now make out through a haze of smoke the Palace of Green Porcelain, and from that I could get my bearings for the White Sphinx. And so, leaving the remnant of these damned souls still going hither and thither and moaning, as the day grew clearer, I tied some grass about my feet and limped on across smoking ashes and among black stems, that still pulsated internally with fire, towards the hiding-place of the Time Machine. I walked slowly, for I was almost exhausted, as well as lame, and I felt the intensest wretchedness for the horrible death of little Weena. It seemed an overwhelming calamity. Now, in this old familiar room, it is more like the sorrow of a dream than an actual loss. But that morning it left me absolutely lonely again—terribly alone. I began to think of this house of mine, of this fireside, of some of you, and with such thoughts came a longing that was pain.
“但是，当我在清晨明亮的天空下，走过冒着烟的灰烬时，我发现自己口袋里还有几根零散的火柴。火柴盒在丢失之前肯定就已经漏了。” ‘But as I walked over the smoking ashes under the bright morning sky, I made a discovery. In my trouser pocket were still some loose matches. The box must have leaked before it was lost.’
第十章 Chapter X
“大约早上八九点的时候，我又走到那个黄色金属座椅的地方。我刚到的那个傍晚就是坐在这个座椅上看着眼前的世界。我想到那天傍晚自己草率得出的结论，忍不住苦笑自己当时的自信。现在，这里的景色还是那么优美，树叶还是那么繁茂，壮丽的宫殿和宏伟的遗迹没有变，那条银光闪闪的河流还是那样流淌在肥沃的河岸间。那些漂亮的人们身穿艳丽长衣在树林里四处活动。有一些人在河里游泳，恰好是在我上次救过威娜的地方，看到这个我心里猛然一阵刺痛。通往地下世界的入口上方的那些圆顶，就像这幅风景画上的斑斑污渍。我现在明白了，上面世界所有这些美好的事物背后掩盖着的是什么。他们的白天很怡人，日子过得就像放养在牧场上的牲畜一样无忧无虑。他们像牲畜一样不知道有任何敌人，不做任何防备，而他们的结局也和牲畜一样。 ‘About eight or nine in the morning I came to the same seat of yellow metal from which I had viewed the world upon the evening of my arrival. I thought of my hasty conclusions upon that evening and could not refrain from laughing bitterly at my confidence. Here was the same beautiful scene, the same abundant foliage, the same splendid palaces and magnificent ruins, the same silver river running between its fertile banks. The gay robes of the beautiful people moved hither and thither among the trees. Some were bathing in exactly the place where I had saved Weena, and that suddenly gave me a keen stab of pain. And like blots upon the landscape rose the cupolas above the ways to the Underworld. I understood now what all the beauty of the Over-world people covered. Very pleasant was their day, as pleasant as the day of the cattle in the field. Like the cattle, they knew of no enemies and provided against no needs. And their end was the same.
“想到人类才智的梦想如此短暂，我不禁悲从中来。是人类的才智亲手扼杀了自己的命运。人类穷尽智力不断追求着安宁和舒适，以实现一个永远安宁的平衡社会为口号。这一希望也曾变成现实——最终却走到了这一步。曾经，生命和财产安全一定都得到了绝对的保障。富人安享他们的财富和舒适，劳动者的生活和工作也得到了保障。毫无疑问，在那个完美的世界中没有失业问题，也不存在亟待解决的社会问题。随之便是天下太平。 ‘I grieved to think how brief the dream of the human intellect had been. It had committed suicide. It had set itself steadfastly towards comfort and ease, a balanced society with security and permanency as its watch word, it had attained its hopes—to come to this at last. Once, life and property must have reached almost absolute safety. The rich had been assured of his wealth and comfort, the toiler assured of his life and work. No doubt in that perfect world there had been no unemployed problem, no social question left unsolved. And a great quiet had followed.
“但有一条自然法则我们忽视了，那就是多方面的才智是对变化、危险和烦恼的补偿。一个和环境相处十分融洽的动物本身就是一个完美的机械装置。只有当习惯和本能都不起作用的时候，自然才会求助于人类的智慧。没有改变和无需改变的地方，也就不会存有智慧。只有那些需要应对各种危险，满足多种需求的动物才会具备一定的智慧。 ‘It is a law of nature we overlook, that intellectual versatility is the compensation for change, danger, and trouble. An animal perfectly in harmony with its environment is a perfect mechanism. Nature never appeals to intelligence until habit and instinct are useless. There is no intelligence where there is no change and no need of change. Only those animals partake of intelligence that have to meet a huge variety of needs and dangers.
“因此，正像我所看到的那样，地上世界的人慢慢变得美丽却很柔弱，而地下世界则走向纯粹的机械工业。但是这种完美状态虽然在机械方面完美无缺，可还是有一点不足，那就是没办法做到绝对的永恒。不管地下世界的食物供给是如何实现的，很明显，随着时间的推移，它出现了空白，变得没有保障了。需求之母被拒之门外了数千年，终于又卷土重来了，而她首先光顾了地下世界。地下生物一直和那些机器打交道，机器无论有多么完美，还是需要他们在习惯之外稍微动点脑筋。虽然他们在其他方面都不如地上居民更具人性，但他们族类的主动性却因此而得以更多地保留。当他们没有其他肉可以吃的时候，旧习惯的戒律被打破。所以我说，这就是802701 年的世界最后一次展示在我眼前时，我所领悟到的情景。这可能是凡人的智力能想出来的再荒谬不过的解释。但是，事实就是这样摆在我眼前的，我只是原模原样地把它描述给你们。 ‘So, as I see it, the Upper-world man had drifted towards his feeble prettiness, and the Under-world to mere mechanical industry. But that perfect state had lacked one thing even for mechanical perfection—absolute permanency. Apparently as time went on, the feeding of the Under-world, however it was effected, had become disjointed. Mother Necessity, who had been staved off for a few thousand years, came back again, and she began below. The Under-world being in contact with machinery, which, however perfect, still needs some little thought outside habit, had probably retained perforce rather more initiative, if less of every other human character, than the Upper. And when other meat failed them, they turned to what old habit had hitherto forbidden. So I say I saw it in my last view of the world of Eight Hundred and Two Thousand Seven Hundred and One. It may be as wrong an explanation as mortal wit could invent. It is how the thing shaped itself to me, and as that I give it to you.
“经历了之前几天的疲劳、兴奋，还有惊恐，尽管我心里还很悲伤，但是眼前这个座椅，宁静的景色，还有温暖的阳光都令人感觉很舒畅。我很累，昏昏欲睡。不一会儿，我就不再分析推理，渐渐打起了瞌睡。我意识到了这点，便心领神会，索性舒展开来躺在草地上，美美地睡了一大觉，以恢复活力。 ‘After the fatigues, excitements, and terrors of the past days, and in spite of my grief, this seat and the tranquil view and the warm sunlight were very pleasant. I was very tired and sleepy, and soon my theorizing passed into dozing. Catching myself at that, I took my own hint, and spreading myself out upon the turf I had a long and refreshing sleep.
“快日落的时候，我醒了。我现在不再担心睡觉时莫洛克斯人会来个突然袭击。我伸伸懒腰，走下山坡，往白色斯芬克斯像那里走去。我一只手里拿着铁棍，另一只手插在兜里玩弄那几根火柴。 ‘I awoke a little before sun setting. I now felt safe against being caught napping by the Morlocks, and, stretching myself, I came on down the hill towards the White Sphinx. I had my crowbar in one hand, and the other hand played with the matches in my pocket.
“这时发生了一件非常意想不到的事情。我靠近那个雕像的底座时，发现那两扇青铜门竟然开着，滑进了下面的门槽之中。 ‘And now came a most unexpected thing. As I approached the pedestal of the sphinx I found the bronze valves were open. They had slid down into grooves.
“看到门开着，我一下子停住了脚步，犹豫着要不要进去。 ‘At that I stopped short before them, hesitating to enter.
“里面是个不大的房间，时光机器就在角落里一个凸起的台子上。机器的小操作杆还在我口袋里。为攻克这个白色雕像，我做了那么多精心的准备。现在，它居然自己乖乖屈服了。我扔掉铁棍，几乎有些遗憾没有用到它。 ‘Within was a small apartment, and on a raised place in the corner of this was the Time Machine. I had the small levers in my pocket. So here, after all my elaborate preparations for the siege of the White Sphinx, was a meek surrender. I threw my iron bar away, almost sorry not to use it.
“我弯腰朝底座里张望的时候，突然想到了一点。至少，有这么一次，我掌握了莫洛克斯人的逻辑。我一边强忍着没有笑出来，一边跨进了底座，登上放时光机器的地方。我惊奇地发现它被仔细地擦拭过了，还上了润滑油。我由此猜出莫洛克斯人甚至曾把它部分拆卸开来，稀里糊涂地想弄清这机器是做什么用的。 ‘A sudden thought came into my head as I stooped towards the portal. For once, at least, I grasped the mental operations of the Morlocks. Suppressing a strong inclination to laugh, I stepped through the bronze frame and up to the Time Machine. I was surprised to find it had been carefully oiled and cleaned. I have suspected since that the Morlocks had even partially taken it to pieces while trying in their dim way to grasp its purpose.
“我站在那里仔细查看我的机器，仅仅是用手抚摸着它都让我感到快乐，就在这时我意料中的事情发生了。入口的青铜板突然滑了上去，哐当一声碰到了上面的门框。我被困在了黑暗之中。莫洛克斯人肯定就是这么认为的。对此我暗暗发笑。 ‘Now as I stood and examined it, finding a pleasure in the mere touch of the contrivance, the thing I had expected happened. The bronze panels suddenly slid up and struck the frame with a clang. I was in the dark—trapped. So the Morlocks thought. At that I chuckled gleefully.
“我已经能听到他们朝我走来时低沉的笑声。我很镇定，试图擦亮一根火柴。只要把那几个操作杆装好，我就会像幽灵一样离去。但是我忽略了一个小细节。我的火柴是只能在火柴盒上点着的那种，真是可恶之极。 ‘I could already hear their murmuring laughter as they came towards me. Very calmly I tried to strike the match. I had only to fix on the levers and depart then like a ghost. But I had overlooked one little thing. The matches were of that abominable kind that light only on the box.
“你们也许可以想象我刚才的镇静如何一下子消失得无影无踪。那些野蛮的小东西已经近在咫尺，有一个还摸了我一下。黑暗中，我用手中的操作杆朝他们横扫过去，并摸着爬进机器座位。接着，前后有两只手触到了我。它们的手指不断夺着我手中的操作杆，我只得一面反击着他们死缠不放的手指，一面摸索着插上操作杆的接口。有一根差点被他们从我手中夺走。就在它快从我手心滑走的时候，我只能用头摸黑去撞，把它夺回来——我能听到那个莫洛克斯人的头骨发出一声清脆的响声。我想，最后的这场争夺战比森林中的那次对决更为惊险。 ‘You may imagine how all my calm vanished. The little brutes were close upon me. One touched me. I made a sweeping blow in the dark at them with the levers, and began to scramble into the saddle of the machine. Then came one hand upon me and then another. Then I had simply to fight against their persistent fingers for my levers, and at the same time feel for the studs over which these fitted. One, indeed, they almost got away from me. As it slipped from my hand, I had to butt in the dark with my head—I could hear the Morlock’s skull ring—to recover it. It was a nearer thing than the fight in the forest, I think, this last scramble.
“但最终，我装好了操作杆，机器启动了。他们黏在我身上的手抽回去了。不久，眼前的黑暗消散了。我发现自己又处于之前描述过的一片灰光和混乱之中。” ‘But at last the lever was fitted and pulled over. The clinging hands slipped from me. The darkness presently fell from my eyes. I found myself in the same grey light and tumult I have already described.’
第十一章 Chapter XI
“前面我已经跟你们说过时光旅行中伴随的恶心和头脑混乱。这一次，我没有坐好，侧着身子坐在上面，不是很稳当。机器不停地摇摆晃动着，我紧紧地贴着它。这样子坚持了不知道有多长时间，完全没注意我是怎么行进的。当我留意去看机器上的表盘时，我惊奇地意识到自己这是到了哪里。有一个表盘显示日数，一个显示千日数，另外还有两个分别显示百万日和十亿日数。现在，我没有反向倒转操作杆，而是把它拉过来，这样就和表盘的记录一起向前进。当我看那些指针的时候，我发现那个千日数的指针就像手表的秒针一样快速旋转——进入未来时空。 ‘I have already told you of the sickness and confusion that comes with time travelling. And this time I was not seated properly in the saddle, but sideways and in an unstable fashion. For an indefinite time I clung to the machine as it swayed and vibrated, quite unheeding how I went, and when I brought myself to look at the dials again I was amazed to find where I had arrived. One dial records days, and another thousands of days, another millions of days, and another thousands of millions. Now, instead of reversing the levers, I had pulled them over so as to go forward with them, and when I came to look at these indicators I found that the thousands hand was sweeping round as fast as the seconds hand of a watch—into futurity.
“向未来行进的过程中，眼前的事物渐渐出现了奇怪的变化。上下跳动的灰色渐渐变得更加黑暗。接着，尽管我仍旧在以极快的速度穿行，我眼前又闪现出昼夜连续的交替。这种情况通常表示速度有所减缓，而且那一明一暗闪烁的交替变得越来越明显。起初我对此大为不解。昼夜的变化越来越慢，太阳在天空划过的进程也更加徐缓，直到最后，它们似乎持续了几个世纪。终于，一道微光恒定地笼罩在大地之上，只是偶尔有一道彗星的眩目光芒划过黑暗的天空，盖过那缕微光。显示太阳运行的那个光带早已消失，因为太阳已经不再东升西落，它仅仅只是在西边上升下落，而且变得越来越大，越来越红，一点也看不到月亮的踪影。星星环绕运行的速度越来越慢，已经变成徐徐移动的亮点。最后，在距我停下来还有一段时间的时候，又大又红的太阳一动不动地停在地平线上。这个巨大的圆球散发出闷热的光，偶尔还暂时性地熄灭一阵。它曾一度又开始照耀起来，而且更为明亮，但是很快又恢复到之前阴沉的赤热状态。看到太阳上升下落的速度渐渐慢下来，我认识到潮汐引力的作用已经消失了。地球的一面朝向太阳静止下来，正如在我们这个时代月亮对着地球一样。我记起上次从机器上一头栽下来，于是开始小心翼翼地刹住机器。指针旋转得越来越慢，直到千日数的那个指针似乎停止了转动，指示日数的指针也不再像之前那样飞速转动，只能看到表盘上模糊一片。速度仍在趋于缓慢，直到最后，一片荒凉海滩的朦胧轮廓呈现在眼前。 ‘As I drove on, a peculiar change crept over the appearance of things. The palpitating greyness grew darker; then—though I was still travelling with prodigious velocity—the blinking succession of day and night, which was usually indicative of a slower pace, returned, and grew more and more marked. This puzzled me very much at first. The alternations of night and day grew slower and slower, and so did the passage of the sun across the sky, until they seemed to stretch through centuries. At last a steady twilight brooded over the earth, a twilight only broken now and then when a comet glared across the darkling sky. The band of light that had indicated the sun had long since disappeared; for the sun had ceased to set—it simply rose and fell in the west, and grew ever broader and more red. All trace of the moon had vanished. The circling of the stars, growing slower and slower, had given place to creeping points of light. At last, some time before I stopped, the sun, red and very large, halted motionless upon the horizon, a vast dome glowing with a dull heat, and now and then suffering a momentary extinction. At one time it had for a little while glowed more brilliantly again, but it speedily reverted to its sullen red heat. I perceived by this slowing down of its rising and setting that the work of the tidal drag was done. The earth had come to rest with one face to the sun, even as in our own time the moon faces the earth. Very cautiously, for I remembered my former headlong fall, I began to reverse my motion. Slower and slower went the circling hands until the thousands one seemed motionless and the daily one was no longer a mere mist upon its scale. Still slower, until the dim outlines of a desolate beach grew visible.
“我十分小心地停了下来，坐在时光机器上，环顾四周。天空不再是蓝色的。东北方向的天空一片漆黑，微白的星星闪耀其中，明亮而又恒定。头顶上的天空是深印度红色，没有星星。东南方向渐渐明亮，变成了鲜艳的红色。巨大的红日，半出于地平线上，一动不动地停在那里。周围的岩石色彩鲜亮，略带红色。岩石朝东南方向突出的部分上面长满了深绿色的植物，这是我最初唯一能看到的生命迹象。那种深绿就跟我们在森林里看到的苔藓或者洞穴里的地衣是一样的：像这样的植物都生长在长期光线微弱的地方。 ‘I stopped very gently and sat upon the Time Machine, looking round. The sky was no longer blue. North-eastward it was inky black, and out of the blackness shone brightly and steadily the pale white stars. Overhead it was a deep Indian red and starless, and south-eastward it grew brighter to a glowing scarlet where, cut by the horizon, lay the huge hull of the sun, red and motionless. The rocks about me were of a harsh reddish colour, and all the trace of life that I could see at first was the intensely green vegetation that covered every projecting point on their south-eastern face. It was the same rich green that one sees on forest moss or on the lichen in caves: plants which like these grow in a perpetual twilight.
“时光机器停在一个有坡度的海滩上。大海向西南方向延伸升起，与天空相接成一条地平线，在暗淡天空的映衬下显得非常明亮。空气中一丝风也没有，没有拍击海岸的巨浪，连波浪也没有。海里只有轻微的起伏，像油一样涌起落下，感觉像是大海微弱的呼吸，显示永恒的大海仍在活动，仍有生命。大海边缘不时地有海水涌出，那里结了厚厚的一层盐，在火红的天空下呈现出粉色。我脑中有种压迫的感觉，而且注意到自己的呼吸也非常急促。这种感觉使我想起我唯一的一次登山经历。由此，我判断这里的空气比我们现在的要稀薄得多。 ‘The machine was standing on a sloping beach. The sea stretched away to the south-west, to rise into a sharp bright horizon against the wan sky. There were no breakers and no waves, for not a breath of wind was stirring. Only a slight oily swell rose and fell like a gentle breathing, and showed that the eternal sea was still moving and living. And along the margin where the water sometimes broke was a thick incrustation of salt—pink under the lurid sky. There was a sense of oppression in my head, and I noticed that I was breathing very fast. The sensation reminded me of my only experience of mountaineering, and from that I judged the air to be more rarefied than it is now.
“从远处荒凉的斜坡上传来一声刺耳的尖叫。一个形似白色巨蝴蝶的东西歪斜着振翅飞起，在空中盘旋，消失在远处低矮的小丘之上。它的声音如此凄厉，听得我浑身颤抖，赶紧牢坐在机器上。再次环顾四周，我发现，之前我以为是一大块淡红色岩石的那个离我很近的东西正慢慢地朝我过来。那东西实际上是一个可怕的像螃蟹似的怪物。你能想象一只螃蟹和那边那张桌子一样大小吗？它的腿很多，缓慢地移动着，步伐不定。它挥舞着大钳子，长长的触须像车夫的鞭子一样在挥动摸索。金属似的面部两侧各有一只叶柄一样的眼睛，冲你闪着微光。在它的背部有一些波浪纹，点缀了许多绿色的斑痕，还有些突起的结疤，看上去十分笨拙。我可以看到，它爬行时结构复杂的嘴里伸出许多触须在扑动摸索。 ‘Far away up the desolate slope I heard a harsh scream, and saw a thing like a huge white butterfly go slanting and f littering up into the sky and, circling, disappear over some low hillocks beyond. The sound of its voice was so dismal that I shivered and seated myself more firmly upon the machine. Looking round me again, I saw that, quite near, what I had taken to be a reddish mass of rock was moving slowly towards me. Then I saw the thing was really a monstrous crab-like creature. Can you imagine a crab as large as yonder table, with its many legs moving slowly and uncertainly, its big claws swaying, its long antennae, like carters’ whips, waving and feeling, and its stalked eyes gleaming at you on either side of its metallic front? Its back was corrugated and ornamented with ungainly bosses, and a greenish incrustation blotched it here and there. I could see the many palps of its complicated mouth flickering and feeling as it moved.
“正当我盯着这个向我爬来的阴险幽灵时，突然感到脸颊上很痒痒，像是有只苍蝇在那里。我试着用手把它擦掉，但是不一会儿，它就又回来了，而且几乎同时耳朵那里又飞来一只。我用手去拍，抓到了一根线状的东西。它很快就从我手里抽了出去。带着极度的疑虑和不安，我转过身来，只见我刚刚抓住的是另一个螃蟹怪物的触须。它就站在我的身后：邪恶的眼睛在肉柄里慢慢地转动，饥饿全写在它的嘴上。它的两个大钳子上沾着海藻的黏液，正笨拙地朝我袭来。我立刻拉动操作杆，向前行进了一个月，但还是在这片海滩上。我一停下来就清楚地看到了那些螃蟹怪物。昏暗中，有几十只这样的怪物在层层鲜绿的叶片间爬来爬去。 ‘As I stared at this sinister apparition crawling towards me, I felt a tickling on my cheek as though a fly had lighted there. I tried to brush it away with my hand, but in a moment it returned, and almost immediately came another by my ear. I struck at this, and caught something threadlike. It was drawn swiftly out of my hand. With a frightful qualm, I turned, and I saw that I had grasped the antenna of another monster crab that stood just behind me. Its evil eyes were wriggling on their stalks, its mouth was all alive with appetite, and its vast ungainly claws, smeared with an algal slime, were descending upon me. In a moment my hand was on the lever, and I had placed a month between myself and these monsters. But I was still on the same beach, and I saw them distinctly now as soon as I stopped. Dozens of them seemed to be crawling here and there, in the sombre light, among the foliated sheets of intense green.
“世界笼罩在一片肃杀荒凉之中，那感觉难以描述。天空，东边是红色的，北边则一片黑暗。含盐的死海；那些肮脏的怪物缓慢地爬行在石滩上；岩石上的苔藓类植物全都是一样的深绿色，看起来像是带有剧毒；伤及肺部的稀薄空气——所有这些景象无不令人心惊胆寒。我又向前驶进了一百年，周围的环境并没有什么变化——那轮红日只是稍微大了一些，暗淡了一些。大海依旧死气沉沉，空气依旧阴冷，陆上那群带壳的怪物仍旧出没在绿色的杂草和红色的岩石之间。西边的天空中，有一道淡淡的弧线，好似一弯巨大的新月。 ‘I cannot convey the sense of abominable desolation that hung over the world. The red eastern sky, the northward blackness, the salt Dead Sea, the stony beach crawling with these foul, slow-stirring monsters, the uniform poisonous-looking green of the lichenous plants, the thin air that hurts one’s lungs: all contributed to an appalling effect. I moved on a hundred years, and there was the same red sun—a little larger, a little duller—the same dying sea, the same chill air, and the same crowd of earthy crustacean creeping in and out among the green weed and the red rocks. And in the westward sky, I saw a curved pale line like a vast new moon.
“地球终极的命运之谜吸引着我继续向前，每跨越一千或一千多年之久我就停一停。眼前的景象令我异常着迷，西边的太阳渐渐变得越来越大，越来越暗，古老地球的生命也逐渐耗尽。最后，在长达三千多万年之后，太阳那个巨大的火球慢慢地模糊暗淡下去，几乎占了黑暗天空的十分之一。随后，我再次停住。地上已经看不到那些四处爬行的螃蟹了，红色的海滩上只剩下青绿色的叶苔和地衣，看起来毫无生气。现在，海滩上布满了白色的斑点，寒意袭人，不时可以看到片片罕见的白色雪花旋转着飘落下来。东北方向天空阴暗，星光照耀下，雪地发出一片亮光。我可以看到粉白色的丘陵轮廓绵延起伏。大海边缘结着一层层的冰，近岸的地方还飘着许多冰块，但是盐海的主海面还没有结冰。太阳永远地落了下去，海面上一片血红。 ‘So I travelled, stopping ever and again, in great strides of a thousand years or more, drawn on by the mystery of the earth’s fate, watching with a strange fascination the sun grow larger and duller in the westward sky, and the life of the old earth ebb away. At last, more than thirty million years hence, the huge red-hot dome of the sun had come to obscure nearly a tenth part of the darkling heavens. Then I stopped once more, for the crawling multitude of crabs had disappeared, and the red beach, save for its livid green liverworts and lichens, seemed lifeless. And now it was flecked with white. A bitter cold assailed me. Rare white flakes ever and again came eddying down. To the north-eastward, the glare of snow lay under the starlight of the sable sky and I could see an undulating crest of hillocks pinkish white. There were fringes of ice along the sea margin, with drifting masses further out; but the main expanse of that salt ocean, all bloody under the eternal sunset, was still unfrozen.
“我环顾四周，看看还有没有任何动物存在的迹象。一种莫名的恐惧使我始终没有离开机器的鞍座。可是，不管是地上、天上，还是海里，我都没有看到任何活动的物体，只有岩石上那些绿色的黏液证明生命还没有消亡。海水已经退离了沙滩，海里出现了一个浅浅的沙洲。我仿佛看到有一个黑色的物体在岸上跳动，但是再仔细看时，它却一动不动了。我断定是自己看花眼了，那个黑色的东西只不过是一块岩石而已。天上的星星非常明亮，看起来似乎不怎么闪烁。 ‘I looked about me to see if any traces of animal life remained. A certain indefinable apprehension still kept me in the saddle of the machine. But I saw nothing moving, in earth or sky or sea. The green slime on the rocks alone testified that life was not extinct. A shallow sandbank had appeared in the sea and the water had receded from the beach. I fancied I saw some black object flopping about upon this bank, but it became motionless as I looked at it, and I judged that my eye had been deceived, and that the black object was merely a rock. The stars in the sky were intensely bright and seemed to me to twinkle very little.
“突然，我意识到太阳西边的轮廓发生了变化，弧线上出现了一个凹面，好似一个小湾，而且凹陷越来越大。大约一分钟，我惊恐地看着眼前黑暗的幕布渐渐遮住了白天。随后，我意识到眼前正进行的是一次日食。月亮或水星正从太阳的圆盘前经过。当然了，一开始我以为是月亮，但是很多迹象使我相信，我看到的实际上是一个内行星凌日的过程，这个内行星经过太阳时，距离地球很近。 ‘Suddenly I noticed that the circular westward outline of the sun had changed; that a concavity, a bay, had appeared in the curve. I saw this grow larger. For a minute perhaps I stared aghast at this blackness that was creeping over the day, and then I realized that an eclipse was beginning. Either the moon or the planet Mercury was passing across the sun’s disk. Naturally, at first I took it to be the moon, but there is much to incline me to believe that what I really saw was the transit of an inner planet passing very near to the earth.
“天色迅速变黑，东边吹来阵阵冷风，让人清醒。空中纷纷扬扬的白色雪花飘落得更加紧密。海边传来潺潺的水声和飒飒响声。除了这些没有生命的声音，世界一片寂静。寂静？真是难以形容那种静。所有的人声、咩咩的羊叫声、鸟鸣声、昆虫的嗡嗡声、耳边熟悉的喧闹声——所有构成我们生活的背景音，现在全都消失了。天越来越黑了，空中旋转的雪花下得越来越密，在我眼前飞舞。空中的寒气更加浓重了。远处小山的白顶终于也一个一个地，一个接着一个地迅速消失在黑暗之中。刚才的微风现在呼啸着呜咽起来。日食当中黑色的阴影向我横扫而来。不一会儿，就只能看到几颗苍白的星星。除此之外，一切都暗淡模糊，天空一片漆黑。 ‘The darkness grew apace; a cold wind began to blow in freshening gusts from the east, and the showering white flakes in the air in creased in number. From the edge of the sea came a ripple and whisper. Beyond these lifeless sounds the world was silent. Silent? It would be hard to convey the stillness of it. All the sounds of man, the bleating of sheep, the cries of birds, the hum of insects, the stir that makes the background of our lives—all that was over. As the darkness thickened, the eddying flakes grew more abundant, dancing before my eyes; and the cold of the air more intense. At last, one by one, swiftly, one after the other, the white peaks of the distant hills vanished into blackness. The breeze rose to a moaning wind. I saw the black central shadow of the eclipse sweeping towards me. In another moment the pale stars alone were visible. All else was rayless obscurity. The sky was absolutely black.
“这茫茫无边的黑暗将我笼罩在恐惧之中。天气的寒冷刺骨和呼吸时感到的疼痛使我不堪忍受。我浑身颤抖着，一阵强烈的恶心涌上来。接着，我看到太阳露出一个火红的弧边。我从机器上下来，想恢复一下精神。我感觉头很晕，无法应付返回的旅程。我站在那里，大脑一片混乱，还觉着恶心。这时，在红色海水中的浅滩上，我又看到了那个活动的东西——现在，我绝对肯定它是活动的。那东西是圆的，跟一个足球大小差不多，或者还要再大一些，长长的触须拖曳着。血红色的海水起伏翻涌，在海水的衬托下，它看起来像是黑色的，时不时地会跳动一下。接着，我感觉自己快要晕倒了，但是想到自己无助地躺在这遥远而可怕的暮色之中，我害怕极了，这种恐惧支撑着我爬上机器。” ‘A horror of this great darkness came on me. The cold, that smote to my marrow, and the pain I felt in breathing, overcame me. I shivered, and a deadly nausea seized me. Then like a red-hot bow in the sky appeared the edge of the sun. I got off the machine to recover myself. I felt giddy and incapable of facing the return journey. As I stood sick and confused I saw again the moving thing upon the shoal—there was no mistake now that it was a moving thing—against the red water of the sea. It was a round thing, the size of a football perhaps, or, it maybe, bigger, and tentacles trailed down from it; it seemed black against the weltering blood-red water, and it was hopping fitfully about. Then I felt I was fainting. But a terrible dread of lying helpless in that remote and awful twilight sustained me while I clambered upon the saddle.’
第十二章 Chapter XII
